Introduction.
Preamble.
Since there is a lack of good masters of this art in our time, it is because medicine is a long field of study, and the author needs to practice dissection before his art with his own hands on the anatomy taught by Galen, until he knows the movements of the members, and their forms, and their connections, and their separations, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, and veins, and their numbers, and their exit, and their palpitations, and quietus, and places of origin.
And for this reason Hippocrates said, 'A name by itself is much, and a work by itself is little, especially in the art of the hand.'
However, we have already spoken about it at the beginning of this book.
Since he who does not know what we have said about anatomy will certainly fall into error, leading to the destruction of humans: as I saw many of them forming a science from it, and boasting about it without knowledge or experience.
That is, because I saw a dull doctor cut the apostema scrofulous wound on the woman's neck, and hit some blood vessels in her throat: why did the woman's blood flow until she died between his hands.
And I saw another doctor who assumed that he would remove a large stone from a man who had been walking for a long time, and the stone was big. So he approached him and removed the vein with a wisp of hair. Why did the man die on the third day?
And I too had been called to extract it; and I saw from a great stone, and from the arrangement of the nurses, that he would die.
And I saw another physician, who was taking a fee from our King for medicine: and it happened that a black eunuch, who was with him, broke his thigh near the heel; and the doctor persued with his ignorance, and bound the fracture together with thin splints and strong bindings, and did not stop the course of the wound's inflammation.
Then he let him go according to his desires. Then after a few days he sent him away and commanded him not to loosen the bindings; and so he remained until his leg and foot had healed properly, but then he came to ruin.
So I was called to loosen the bindings; and what followed was peace, and he was freed from his pain.
But the corruption had already taken hold in the limb; and I could not prevent it.
Then the corruption ceased to spread in the limb until he died.
And I saw another physician who opened a cancerous boil; and it became ulcery after a few days, until the malignancy spread to his lord.
That is, for when it is cancerous from the melancholic humor, then one should not approach it with iron at all unless it is present in a member that can bear it, so that it may be cut off entirely.
And for that reason, O sons, you must know that the art of surgery is divided into two parts: that which is associated with health, and that which is associated with danger in many arrangements.
And I too have already set forth in every part of this book wherever surgery has come up, where there is terror and fear.
Why do you need to tell him that, and to decrease it? So that the dumb fool doesn't offend me with his words and dishonors me.
Therefore, receive with care and protection, and bring our sick with ease and strength, and use a better path, led by the grace of God to salvation and worthy succession: and remove from us that which makes us fear, so that it may enter upon us hesitation in our faith and our comfort.
For it remains more to remain in our glory, and higher in the world, and at last to the quantities of us.
Because Galen has already said in some of his adages. Do not cure disease with medicine: do not name a doctor to disease.
But I have already divided this treatise into three chapters.
Chapter one.
Chapter on cauterization with fire and medication, on acute medication, on medicine that is hot or cold, on the shape of instruments and tools for cauterization, and on everything else needed in the operation.
Chapter two.
On cutting and piercing, phlebotomy and wound-cleaning, and extracts of arrows, and similar things: and the whole chapter on the shape of instruments.
Chapter three.
On restoration, dislocation, and cure for torsion, and similar things: the whole chapter, ordered from head to foot, and with the shapes of instruments.
But before I remember the operation with him, it is necessary that I should tell you the quality of his cauterization and non-cauterization: and in which complexion he shows it.
I therefore say that the speech on the quality of cauterization and its harm is long, subtle, scientific, and secret.
Also spoken was a great number of wise men, and they disagreed with each other; but for me, little of their words is sufficient, fearing the lengthiness of their speech.
I therefore say that cauterization is universal to all complexions, whether with or without substance; excepting two complexions, which are a hot, substance-less complexity and a dry, substance-less complexity.
In complexity, however, hot and dry with substance, they disagreed. Some, indeed, have said that cauterization is useful in that. And others said the opposite of that, namely that cauterization is not suitable for an illness which is hot and dry: for fire's nature is hot; and it is unsuitable, as it heals a hot and dry illness with hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite of that said: That by cauterization healing is done in any hot and dry illness which occurs in human bodies; for when you compare a human body, and its moisture, to the complexity of fire, the body's coldness disappears.
And I myself say by that speech: for by experiment I have discovered that at times.
However, it is not necessary that you make that point, except those who have already been tested and exercised in the last exercise of the chapter on cauterization, and have recognized the diversity of human complexions, and the nature of illnesses within them, and their causes, and their accidents, and the time period of their existence.
From the other complexities there is no fear for you; and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all doctors have already agreed upon them; and they did not disagree on cauterization in them.
And know ye sons, that the secret of cure by cauterization with fire, and the goodness thereof, is when the medicine is burned with the fire upon the cautery: for fire is simple, whose action does not reach, unless to the member which is cauterized; and does not hurt the other member joined therewith, unless with a little injury.
But the action of medicine when it is burned and increased by fire reaches that which extends from the members: and perhaps makes it happen to a member that it has difficulty in being cured, and perhaps destroys it.
But fire because of its subtlety and goodness of its substance does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now this has already become known to us by trial, because of the length of practice and study with art and standing on the veracity of things: and because of this excuse from the length of speech.
And if it were not, because it is not allowed to this my book, I would give you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its action on the bodies by means of its expulsion: which expels diseases with a philosophical demonstration-phrase, which was added by the minds of your ancestors.
And know ye sons, that yourselves differ in the time when it is to be made to happen cautery, and put a better time of medicine:
And I say that cautery is suitable at all times: for the injury which happens because of time is hidden in a good will, which is attracted with the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary pains, firming, banquets which do not tolerate delay: for they are afraid of them, that a bad will happen which is greater than a little injury is to blame for the lack of time.
And do not fall into the minds of your sons that they should not judge, except for common and stupid doctors, namely that he who is cured of a disease by cautery does not always recover: and they put its consequence, and it is not like what they think: for cautery is not, unless in place of medicine, which changes the complexion, and dries up humidities which are the causes, wherefore pains happen.
Indeed, the cautery is superfluous on top of the medicine due to its velocity, vigor, and power, and because it belongs to the Lord: and it is possible that the sickness be restored at some time during the course of nursing, and location of sickness, and strength; and that it is prepared in his body from an excess that has accumulated in him: and that it comes to him in its acquisition from food, and similar things from causes, unless there is sickness, in which cauterization is administered.
Indeed, a slight sickness in a small member is superfluous due to excess dryness and humidity, like the pain of a tooth, for its own pleasure, and other similar things; because it is possible that this pain does not return to him. But that is true only in a few cases.
But the word of the cure is again true; that the cautery is last of all medicine, it is a straight word: not to that which they intend in him; for they believe that there is no healing with medication, nor with anything else after the occasion of the cautery.
But the case is just the opposite, and the intention, that the cautery is last of all medicine, is not true; unless when we administer methods of cure in some diseases, and do not give them medicine: then we administer at the end of the matter a cautery, and it comes to pass. Then it falls, that the cautery is last of all medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many medical doctors understand.
But the ancient ones have said that a gold cautery is better than an iron one: and they did not say that, except for the equality of gold, and the limitation of its substance; and they have said that it does not make a wound in the cauterizing place. But that is not absolutely so; for I have tested that, and found that it does not make those wounds in certain bodies without others.
It is good to use the cautery with it, and better than using iron, as they say. Indeed, when you use the fire cautery on gold, it does not show you, when lit according to the quantity you use, due to the redness of the gold: and when it is proper for it to be cold, and if you add ignition on top of it, it melts in the fire and turns into leaves.
Why does the craftsman fall from that [practice]: and for that reason we prefer the cautery with iron among us, and more quickly and closer to the work, from truth to operation.
And I have already arranged this chapter on the cautery, according to the chapters: and I have arranged it from the head until the feet: so that you may find what you want from it.
Chapter II.
Confirm here the cauterization to the domain of humidity and coldness on the brain: which are two causes of salt, and a multitude of flow of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and a multitude of sleep, and pain of teeth, and pain of throat: and generally all sickness that happens from coldness, such as paralysis, and salting, and epilepsies, and apoplexies, and similar things from those illnesses.
The way of cauterization is, so that you prescribe to the sick: that it be drained in the first place with a solute and purifying medicine, washing the head three nights, or four, according to what the power of the sickness, and its age, and custom, demand.
Then prescribe to him that he should wash his head with a soft cloth. Then make him sit between your hands, so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. So whenever your middle finger has come up to that point with uneasiness, mark that spot with an unclean mark.
Then fire cautery: this is its shape.
Then put the flesh on the marked spot with your fingers, and squeeze it gently, and then remove it. Then quickly wipe your hand, and examine the spot.
If you see now a little quantity of salt on the bone, or a little quantity of licorice, then quickly wipe your hand. And if not, repeat the motion with the iron, or with another one when it is chilled: until you see the bones, which I told you.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and immerse the cloth in it, and put it on the spot: and leave it for three days.
Then put on the spot the cloth immersed in butter, and leave it until the fire is completely extinguished. Then take care of that with the four-fold ointment until it heals.
They have already said that since the wound remains open for so long, pus is emitted: why is it better and more helpful?
And some of them said, to cauterize the skin all the way down to the bone: and hold the cautery until a certain hardness is achieved.
Then clean after that what has been burned, then cauterize it.
And others say that it is necessary to do with the cautery what I have just described, so that an impression of a knot is made on the bone: or the instrument which women put in their hair with a little letter: and they cut off, that vapours of the head's essence may be emitted from this place, and the wound may heal after a long time.
Then cauterize it until it hardens.
But these two species of cautery do not seem to exist among all men, except for certain people from second-hand knowledge out of fear.
And leave it: as far as I am concerned, it is better with the health of that person.
For the head is weakened by the resolution of its natural continuity; as we have testified in the other members; and above all when the head is weak, by nature: and the species of cautery is more sound and better with me, and I use it; so let us operate on it while it is healthy.
Chapter III: On the Mode of Causing a Head W
When in the whole head there is a chronic pain; and when it is prolonged in an invalid, and if he uses hypos, hot baths, head rinsings, oils, and applications: then operate. And especially if already cauterized with one kind of cautery which we have described, and gives it no benefit: then consider. For if the head is weak by nature's creation, and is not weak, and cold is keen: then cauterize with another kind of cautery a little below it. Then cauterize itself on all the horns of its head with its own cautery, and do not let the skin be burned, and uncover a quantity from the bone, which we have described. And cauterize itself with one kind of cautery at the back of its head, in the place which is called the vein; and this is a place where there is a flowing wind: and moisten your palm well in this, and do not uncover the bone. For an invalid will have keen pain because of this, and is far removed from the pain of the other parts of the head's cauterization.
And I will call this cautery in its place; and it should be that by which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of the head by a finer cautery, by which the middle of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV: On Causing a Head to Bleed When it has
When pain and swelling occurs in part of the head, or when the pain extends to the eye, and if the head is washed with medicinal solutions, and the remaining treatment is given, as I have described in the divisions of diseases, and this does not benefit him entirely: then cauterization must be done in two ways: either cauterization with a sharp medicine that burns; or with iron.
But if cauterization is to be done with a sharp medicine that burns, i.e., take one of the teeth of another, and cut it out, and cut off its ends from the two sides. Then cut the place of pain at the time with a phlebotome on the side, until it is made into a place under the skin, in which a lump is captured.
Then introduce it into him under the skin, until it is hidden: then tie it over it with a knot of constrictive yarn, and leave it for fifteen hours, and then dissolve it, and pull out one, and leave it for two days, or three: then put a cloth over the spot immersed in butter, until a pus place forms: then care for the wound with ointment until it heals.
And if you want to make it with some sharp medicines that burn, which I have written about in the second book, On Burning Medications.
But cauterization with iron is according to this method. Fire Cauterization, whose form is this:
And it is called a Clavicle: because the form of the head is like the form of a clavicle, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it is a small eminence.
Then place the iron on the spot, and hold your hand: and you will turn the iron gradually with speed: and let the amount that burns be of the thickness of the skin, such as half of it. And raise your hand so that the artery below does not burn, and an outflow of blood does not occur.
Then dip the wound in saline water and put it on the place and leave it for three days; then put the wound with butter: later care with ointment until healed.
And if you see, cauterize this headache with an edge of scalpel second cautery. And do not cut the artery in this half-headache, but old one his own.
The mode of cauterizing in an old headache.
When you treat a headache, with what we have said before in the preceding cure, and that which we have said in the divisions of diseases, and there is no cure: and you see from the disease that it does not suffice to him what we have said from the first cauterization with medicine, or with cauterization with fire, then it must be that you bring the fires of Cauterie, until it becomes white after the signs on the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or almost like it: and put your hand out one way, and squeeze it until you touch the artery, and reach as far as the mouth.
However, it is necessary for you, so that you cauterize the continuation of the jaw, which moves when chewing, does not burn on the side, or nerve that moves it, from which happens a spasm.
And be on guard, and beware of the flow of blood of the artery, which is cut off. For there is a fear in the cutting off of it, and especially to him who does not know what he does, and is not learned, nor expert: and dismisses the operation with it at first.
And I come with a reminder of the regime of the flow of blood from an artery according to its own way, and in its place in this book.
That if you see from the disease that this cauterization is not sufficient for him, and you see the body bearing the cauterization in the middle of the head, as we have told, care about the sore, until it heals.
And if you see, administer cautery, which we have said in the chapter on arteriotomy with a cautery having two scalpels. For cauterization is better and more effective in this way.
§ On the method of cauterizing in ear pain.
When it happens that there is pain in the ear from cold, and cauterize with water, and the rest of the cure as we have said in the division, and the pain does not disappear, then fire Cautery: and that is what is called a point, whose form is this.
Then the points with it after its ignition around the whole ear, as it swells: or in the circumference of each, if at the same time pain is in both. And stretch it with the cautery from the root of the ear slightly, after you have marked the places with wax: and let the quantity of cauterium be ten points all over the ear, and almost the same.
Then care for the place, until they are healed.
§ On the method of cauterizing in torture.
Chapter VII.In cumque cauterium ignis fac
For the torture which is cured with cauterization, is not except for the kinds that happen from phlegm, according to what we have said in divisions of diseases.
And prolonged cauterization of a species that happens from drying up, and the spasm of a nerve.
When you treat this species of torture with hyoscyamus, and caputpurums, and gargarisms, and your cure does not bring about a result, then you should cauterize the sick three times: one near the root of the ear, and a second slightly below its place, and a third at the meeting of the two lips.
And put your cautery on the opposite side of the weak part. For softening does not happen except in the part that appears to be healthy.
And the form of cauterizing is so that it cauterizes itself with the cautery in the direct extremity of the upper ear near the hairline slightly: and another in the time: whose length is according to the length of the finger. And lay your hand with the cautery, until the amount of half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery; and it has a kind of blade whose form is as follows: indeed, it is not too fine, as you see; and it is necessary that the blade should be somewhat thin, because of its thickness.
Then take care of the wound with this; until such time as it heals: unless you want to suffer a great deal of pain and loss.
(On the way of cauterizing in ancient apoplexia.)
When apoplexia is old, and you take care of it with that which I have said, and your medicine does not avail, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every corner of his head, and with one in the middle of his head, as we have said, and with one at the back of his head, according to what preceded: and let the mode of the cautery be according to what preceded.
Also cauterize with the cautery on the mouth of the stomach: and it is more the last.
Then take care of it with that which preceded.
CHAPTER IX.
It is necessary that they be given to the first patient with great fever, and pills that clean the brain.
Then cut off his head entirely, and put on his scalp an ointment described in the book of ointments: and apply it sometimes.
This is the way to make a poultice: and do it according to the order which I have mentioned there.
If then he recovers by means of it, it is good. If not: then do to him three cauterizations in the posterior part of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and put between every cauterization a thickness of finger.
Then take care of the poultice, with what preceded it.
If however you want to add something, and the sick man endures that: then do to him a cauterization in the middle. That if you want to add something: then cauterize him over two horns.
Then take care of the head until it is healed: and let the poultice be oiled according to the form which I have mentioned above.
As to the way of cauterizing in paralysis and softening.
Head
It is necessary that you proceed in cleaning out the head with fever, and with what I have said.
Then cut off the head and nurse it: then cauterize him in the middle of the head, and on all the horns of the head, and on the posterior part of it, and three on the spine of the neck.
If however you are not able to endure the softening of the body in many places, and the sick person endures that and the illness is strong: then cauterize him with four cauterizations on the spine of the back, and the last one while it is burning up from his skin, and wash your hand. Then take care of the head until it is healed: and let the poultice be oiled in this way.
As to the way of cauterizing in epilepsy.
He should not cauterize an epileptic patient unless he is certain that the epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, to begin with, he should wash out his brain with water and with the other remedies which we have mentioned in the section on general treatment; for a sick man is great or tolerant of medicine.
But if he is a boy who does not tolerate medicines, then let him be given gargles and mouthwashes to wash out the brain; before many days of good diet.
Then rinse his head, and afterwards cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of his head, and according to what has been said before in the method; and another cautery on his occiput, and over all the ridges of his head. If the sick man is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the medicines which I have mentioned for paralysis and softening of the body on the neck and back; and let there be olive oil as a second method of cautery.
But if the sick man is a boy, then place the fine cautery, according to this method:
The way of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupt moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the medicines which we have mentioned for paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of vapor going into melancholy, and his body is wet with moisture; then give him in a vessel which washes out his brain, according to what has been said in the division: and afterwards rinse his head, and then make a loop made loosely of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of his head: and let the sick man sit holding himself upright.
Then present the liniment. And it is more honorable from old butter. Let him heat him on a moderate fire; and let him put his hand into him when he bears the heat, as he enters into him. Then he cleared him out in the middle of his head in a circle, and let him go until he became cold.
Then let him have this treatment once a week with the rest of the regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you want to put a ring around him, a small circle of fire, except that you hold your hand with the cauldron: and let it emit odour.
This kind of fire moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place a cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat, on him.
The way of treating with fire going down to the eye.
Chapter 13:
When you see the beginning of the water in the eye, which I mentioned in the division, then begin to drink and make the sick person drink, so that he may refresh his head.
And keep him away from all moisture, and let him sit in a bath, on a few days' fast.
Then command him to wash his head, and let him treat himself with fire in the middle of his head. Then let him treat himself with fire on either side of the head with two torches, if the beginning is the descent of water into both eyes at once: or from one side, if the beginning is the entrance of water into one eye: and cut off with the torch all the veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let there be torches long in length. And let him guard against the flow of blood.
If you see anything of this, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting off, and their carefulness against the flow of blood.
And whenever he is treated with fire in wax, under two bones, with two torches at the end.
The way of treating with fire in ancient tears:
When the tears of the eyes are ancient and constant, and they are on the veins, and the arteries that are in the front of the head, it is certain that it is from cold and phlegm: then let him treat himself with fire by means of the same torch that I mentioned at the beginning of the entrance of water, a fire in the middle of the head, and two torches on either side of the head, and two torches in wax under two bones. And if it does not heal with addition, then cauterize him in all sides carefully the eye, on the extremity of the superciliary arch with a small cautery.

In the cauterium but with fire: however, before that, recommend that he stops his hairs from coming off, if he is of those who wash them, until they grow out and become even. If I puncture him near his eye: then constrict his eyes with putty, so that they do not move until they have healed.
When they have healed and been brought to a steady state, then place the head of the patient in your lap: afterwards mark the eyelids of his eyes with caustice, a mark that is shaped like a leaf of myrrh: and let the mark begin from near the hair.
Then place a damp cloth soaked in albumen, or in a slippery substance made from the mucilage of psyllum, on the eye.
Then apply fire to the mark, its shape being this:
Then cauterize over the mark, slowly and repeatedly, until the surface of the skin is completely burnt away, leaving a shape that resembles the leaf of myrrh, all by itself.
And the mark of your work is this: so that if you press the eyelids of his eyes together, and feel the hair near the mark of the wound, you will know that the patient's eye has been healed.
So then let go of your hand, and send him away for a few days.
Then place on the patient's skin a cloth soaked in butter, until the scar is removed. Then tend to the patient with ointment, until he is healed.
If any of his hair falls out an hour later and the eyelid becomes soft, then apply fire to the same place as before, as you did in the beginning.
If, however, the hair has fallen out at the lower eyelid, then cauterize that place until it has returned to its natural position: and make sure that the eyes do not tickle after.
It is as you command for the sick person: let him forgo shaving his hair, until it has grown and settled down. Make in the shape of a leaf of myrrh out of a piece of cloth or a patch of linen.
Then take out of a known soap, and from a clay that is not soaked in any weight or almost like it: then rub it together with good rubbing, and make it with speed, so that it does not grow cold. Then from that take a piece, and put it on the paper that you made like the form of an oak leaf, and place [it] on the eyelid of one eye or two eyes. And put under the eye a cotton wodge soaked in albumin or: and let the head of the patient lie in your lap.
And put your finger like an index on the medicine, and press it a little. And you move [it] whenever the sick person feels a tingling sensation from the medicine: for its bite is like fire.
While he was persisting in doing so because he found the bite of the medicine, then let go of the medicine, and move  [it] yourself with your finger. While he was calming down from the bite, then let go of the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid close up, like it closes during burning or incising, is good: and if not, then repeat again on top of that place from the medicine where it does not impress the medicine, and does not harm, until your operation is completed, and the eye closes.
Then put on the eye a cotton wodge with butter, until the skin of the burn is peeled off. Then take care of the eye with a diaphenicon ointment, or any other, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you near the operation, to guard the last guards, so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
That if the eyelid softens after a few days, and fights with some hair in the eye, then repeat again on that place the medicine where it softens from the eyelid of itself, like you did in the beginning. Then take care of the eye, until it heals.
And this is the form of an oak leaf.
And you should know that human eyes differ from each other in size and shape. So therefore according to this consideration be your thought: and do not conceal the straightness of its direction, which is the study of this art.
To cauterize a lacrimal fistula.
When you treat a fistula, as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help: then you should cauterize it according to this method.
Order the sick person to put his head in your lap, and hold his head between your hands so that he does not move or shake it.
Then put the cotton wisp soaked in alumen, or in mucilage of psillium, on his eye; then hold it over the fire, which should be shaped like this.
Sit facing the fire, as the shape of a flute's feather extends from one end, so that it is heated on one side; and if the wisp sits so as to penetrate all the way to the other end, and if the wisp sits so as to be held up towards the sky.
However, this kind of fire is better suited to your purpose.
Then express the fistula if it is open, and remove anything from it, and dry it out; and if it is not open, then open it and remove any pus from it.
Then put the fire on it, which should burn fiercely.
And hold it with your hand somewhat near the fire, towards the nose, so that your hand does not move or shake the sick person; and place the fire on the eye fat, and dissolve it.
If then you see any pus at the beginning of your fire up to the mouth, it is good. And if not: then repeat the fire once or twice, if you can bear it; and discharge him after three days.

That if he does not heal after fourty days, then put on him an acute corrosive medicine until the mouth is detected; and cut it according to what it says in his own chapter.

[On the mode of cauterizing the liver.]
When an ulcer is seen to be coming out, and you need to know if it is in the liver or in its membrane: then if it is in the liver, you will see a dull pain, and there is a mild acuteness: and you will see that the treatment of the doctors for it tires them out.

And this is its form. Then place the coal on the wool, and leave it until it goes out. Then repeat this. So do not stop doing that, until the sense has become accustomed to the mediation up to the ankle, and the pain has rested.
And this method of cautery is called Vaccinium cautery.

When this podagra of cold cause is cured with modes of curing, and the pains do not move away, then remove the cautery to move them.

And if you can stand as dots on the face of the foot, then do it with a dot of cauldron. That if they ascend pains up to the knees, or other joints, and often this happens: then cauterize him over all knee with four cauldron, or six from every part, with this same cauldron of Olive oil.
If, however, you need more of this remedy, then cauterize him then. And do not submerge your hand with the caustic, but rather sit around it with only the spiciness of the skin.
If, however, the pains rise up to the knees, and the back: then administer what we said above from the caustic in our chapter.
That if the pains are only in the hands, then poke around with fire, as they return like two lines.
If, however, there remains any pain in the fingers, then poke them, over every lump a point, and over the palm of the hand.
If, however, the pains rise up after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both of them from all parts.
And do not let the sick person recover from a good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if the regimen is made good, and the phlegm is excreted, it will be healed by the help of God with this caustic.
On the Manner of Causing a Burn to Heale Broken Bones.
When a Rupture has occurred in the groin, and has descended into the bowels, or to the testicle, and it is beginning to be near to the scrotum: then you shall order the sick person to cease from food in his own day. And let him use laxatives, so that the dung may descend from his own gut.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back: and order him that he hold his breath until he has gone forth, or show his buttocks, or his intestine.
Then let him reduce the man with your fingers, and mark with the caustic under a Rupture on the top of the pelvis, with the sign whose end is similar to half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then let the caustic fire be held, with this form, until it has become white, and throw off sparks. Then let the intestine be reduced, or the buttocks to its cavity. Then let the attendant place his hand upon the place so that he does not exit the intestines: and you have already opened between the ribs of the sick person, and placed under it the penis, and one servant stands on his ribs, and another on his chest who holds the hands.
Then let him deposit the caustic on the spot, with your hand holding the caustic upright. And hold him, until you are satisfied with him: or else go again with him by another route, if you are not satisfied with him in the first place up to the mouth.
And carefully observe that there is no exit from the intestines at the time of your cauterization, so that he does not burn himself, and let him go through it to the sick or to death, or great mischief.
And know that when you do not achieve the mouth with the caustic, your operation is fruitless.
And it should be that the caustic of infants is subtle, according to their measure.
Then care for him with the rest of the ointment, until he recovers.
And let the sick person lie on his back for forty days, until the wound is closed.
And let him take food by length of time of his cure, which softens his gut: so that he does not exit the intestines through desire and defecation.
Then when he should rise after forty days, then give him a looser ligature, and let him hold for forty more days.
And let him abstain from work, and be filled with food and drink, and loud speeches.
For when he uses this regimen, he is healed by a whole cure.
And I will tell the cure of ruptures with an incision in its chapter.
When, however, ruptures occur in the remaining gut, and are incipient, and do not enter, then cauterize his rupture with your round caustic according to its quantity: and let it be what is burned from then on as the third one. Then take care of yourself, as we have said: and do not be led astray.
And some have said first: that it should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this form.
Afterwards sign it with encaustic, and place the line which is across from the lateral upper part of the rupture, and another line towards the bottom. And put your hand in the middle with the cautery closed.
But it is easier and better to use the cautery first.
The mode of cauterizing in pains by accident, or by percussion.
Chapter LXVIII.
When it happens in some member by accident, or by percussion: and that pain persists a long time, and does not respond to treatment with medicines: then it should be cauterized with the Pointed cautery.
And let the cautery be to all members according to its size, and its health, and its weakness, and its virtue, and its location of twist, and the pain from it.
But if it is healed by the first cauterization, it is good. If not: then repeat on top of it the cauterization.
For these pains are used to pass from one member to another as it approaches that which is affected. Why should the consequences be caused by the cautery, until the sick is healed.
The mode of cauterizing in Leprosy.
But the lepers should be cauterized by a sharp instrument. And especially the characteristic of Leprosy, which is caused by putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: so that you consider carefully how to cauterize it.
If this Leprosy is not open, and you have treated it with the one we have mentioned in the division, and it has not come down, nor stayed: and you wait for the disease to encompass the whole complexion: then cauterize him on top of the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the hairline, and a second lower down towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two above the two ears, and one behind the nape of the neck.
And last, you shall hold your hand with the cautery just a little while, until it prints upon the mouth an impression of pallor, and the membranes are displaced from it; that the expiration of the vapors of great heat may be relieved, and the cautery also over the splenetic organ, according to what went before.
But if the leper has already spread on the sick person and appears clearly: then you shall cauterize with these cauteries which we said in the beginning, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the two cheeks, and two cauteries on the two sides of the neck, and six on the sides of the back, and one great one on the hahosas near the tail end and one above it: and two on the shoulders and two on the elbows, and two on the breasts, and one on the entire chest, from the connection of the fingers of his hands and feet: and cauterize him on all joints, from the connection of the fingers of his hands and the feet of his feet: and cauterize him on all heels of his feet, and on the knuckles of his hands.
And so that you do not burn them, take care from the nerves that are at the very end of the heel.
And when one is cauterized with a cautery on the bone of the chest, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And you should know that the more you add cautery, the greater is the benefit, and the more it confers.
And you should know that a sick person does not feel pain in the cautery, unlike a healthy person: therefore because his body is already stunned.
And it is fitting that the cauteries should be of a size and proportion appropriate to the limbs and joints: according to what went before from the appearance of the tools of the trade.
Then care for the cauteries with flour of herb and honey, and with the rest of the cure, until it is healed.
To cauterize in a stupor.
When a limb is stuporous and does not heal with medicines, oils, plasters, and so on, then cauterize the limb that is stuporous with cautery, according as the magnitude of the limb is increased, or its diminutio
And place your cautery instrument within the thickness of the skin a little. Then care for the limb with ointment until it is healed.
And sometimes when cauterization occurs for some stupefaction which befalls the hand, or foot, in the spine of the back near the exit of nerves which stir that limb: and the stupefaction is removed.
But he does not do this [cauterization] unless he is wise in the anatomy of limbs, and knows the exit of nerves which stir the body.
Head.

The way to cauterize in cancer.Caput LII.
When cancer is beginning, and the eye is affected: then cauterize the eye with a circular cautery according as it turns.
But the wise have said, that the last cautery in the middle should be used.Et quandoque cauterizatur, non facit utrique oculo, sed mediocoelo, et postea
But to me that does not seem right: for I fear that it will ulcerate: and I have seen it sometimes.
And it is better that he be cauterized around his wound with a circle, as we have said: or with many caustics.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in ablation.
When someone has ablation and it is delayed in maturing, or because of superfluous reasons that cause it, or because of old age, when the blood is little, or because of time, and the pulse rushes to mature ablation, then cauterize around his wound with a few caustics by pricking. Then let go of him. For it will hurry with the maturation.
But if you pierce his wound with a caustic, then take this kind of caustic, which is in the form of:
And place him in the middle of the ablation until it enters the skin; and let the caustic remain with him because it will weaken, so that the flow of blood may be eased.
Then take care of him until he is healed.
Regarding the method of cauterizing with a caustic that corrupts.
Chapter III. On Corrupted Wounds.
Corrosion is not but corruption in a walking member, and it corrupts the member itself; just as fire consumes dry wood.
But if you see corrosion in a place that tolerates caustic with fire, then take many caustics, small and large, as is suitable for the place where corrosion is.
Then cauterize him from all parts until you eradicate the entire corruption, and do not leave any trace of it.
Then let him go for three days, and place sulfur, reduced with oil, on the cauterized places until all the eschar and corruption are eradicated.
Then take care of him with ointments that generate flesh.
But if you see that after three days healthy flesh is born by a kind of rebirth, and there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then apply cautery to that which remains in the corrupted locations.
And sometimes when it is infected it is cured with acute medicine. For it itself rises up at the place of cauterization.
However, cauterization with fire is faster in effect: and I have indeed already said that cauterization with acute medicine is applied in division: so take it there when it tolerates it.
On the method of cauterizing in slits and warts.
Chapter 50.
This disease often occurs in the lower parts of the feet: and it is a gross, filter-like growth that hurts the foot.
And there are two ways of applying cauterization to them: cauterization with fire and cauterization with hot water.
As for the cauterization with fire, like the feathers of a penning torch it is prepared from iron, according to the quantity that contains the clap when all parts are covered: and its edge should be sharp.
Then place the burned thing on the clap. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the clap, until the cauterization reaches the depth of the clap: and leave it for three days, until pus begins to be discharged. Then bind the thing with wet silkworm threads, crushed with salt: and leave the plaster on the thing at night. For it itself will be eradicated from its roots.
Then care for the place with a soft salve of meat, until it heals.
If they are not turned inside out and often occur on the surface of the body, especially on the hands and feet: then apply to them cauterization with hot water: and it is like receiving a tube made of brass, iron, or a feather of a penning torch: and place it on the clap, or on an atharel. Then pour into the tube a little amount of hot water: hold your hand so that it is turned around with your finger to such an extent that the edge of the tube is pressed into the root of the clap, and the hot water is found at the bottom: and let stand for a while on the prickling of the hot water.
Then release him, for the wound to be cured with its roots.
So do with them one after another until you have done all that are in the body.
Then take care of them after they have been eradicated, with the same unguent that generates flesh from the wax.
The method for cauterizing in a tremor.
When it happens to someone who has a tremor due to cold in a nerve, or from quartan fever, or otherwise: then you should cauterize the spot four times, or five on top of the spine, and between each vertebrae with cautery, and in the pit of the stomach with cautery, and above the stomach with cautery.
For a tremor ceases when it is oiled with cauterization, and a feverish health is hastened by the health of cold.

The method for cauterizing in a flux of blood from an artery in the ulnar:
However, it often happens that a flux of blood comes from an artery that has been cut near the ulnar, whether from outside, or at the site of an abscess, or when cauterizing a member, and similar things: and it is difficult to stop it. Oportet itaque ex parte, ubi accidit, aduersus haec caute
So when this happens to someone, then grasp the affected artery with your hand and place your finger over it as an indicator: and grip it very tightly until the blood is stopped under your finger and nothing comes out of it.
Then put on a small amount of olive oil fire, and a great many more: and blow on them until they are very hot.
Then take from them one, or small, or large, according to the size and place of the broken artery, and place the fire on it: then remove your hand quickly: and hold the fire until the blood is completely stopped.
If you should release your hand from the opening of the artery and put out the fire, then take another fire quickly from those that are prepared in the fire:
So do not stop doing this with one after the other until the blood is completely stopped.
And be careful so that you do not burn the fire that is there, and do not bring on another injury to a healthy person.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, it is then impossible to stop it: especially if the artery is large, unless with four fingers. Or with fire, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is extracted, its ends are drawn back, and the blood stops flowing. Or it is bound with a strong knot of thread. Or are placed on the top of a drug that stops the flow of blood and is tightened with a decreasing constriction.
But he who gives the cut with a knot, and constriction with a cloth, or puts burning things together, and similar things, does not give it deeply unless rarely.
But if this happens to someone and there is no present physician or medicine: then begin with the position of the index finger over the opening of the wound, as we have related, and its constriction very tightly until the blood is stopped from the upper part of the wound, and around the artery. And the finger should not be moved away, above it with cold water always stirring the cold, until the blood has congealed, and has thickened, and has been cut off.
And while that is considered, what does not require a poultice or medicine.

Of the treatment of water which is added to the heads of boys.
Chapter I.
You should know that this sickness often occurs in boys at birth; or when the midwife squeezes the head of the boy without gentle touch.
And whenever it also happens for an unknown cause which is not known.
And I have not seen this disease in any other than in boys; and I wished to see all of them die, because of that, therefore I have left off the operation on it.
And I have seen a boy from among them, of whom the head was filled with water, and his head increased in size every day, until he could not sit himself up on his own, because of the size of his head: and his moisture increased, until he died.
And this moisture, or it is added between the skin and the jaw: or it is added under the bone over the Mandible.
And the operation in that, if there is humidity between the skin and bone, and the apostema is small, then you should find a fissure in the middle of the head in width; and its length be almost two knots until the humidity has run out.
And this is the form of the scalpel.
But if the humidity is increased and the apostema is larger, then place two fissures according to this form.
But if the humidity is under the bone and the sign of it is that you see the comissures of the head open from all parts: and the water is depressed when you press it with your hand towards the inside, and is not hidden from you: then you should find in the middle of the head three fissures, according to this manner.
And after the incision, remove all the humidity. Then tighten the fissures with rags and flour. Then dip it in vinegar and oil until the fifth day.
Then dissolve the ligaments, and care for the wounded joints with linen, and ointments.
And do not cease to tighten the head with equality. And feed the sick with dry and little-humidity food until their member is comforted, and healed.
And another way of incision is that you consider where the appearance of the size of the apostema and the collection of water appears.
Since when ever it is in the back more, or in the front, or on the right, or on the left.
So climb up with an incision where you see the apostema and the filling appear: and cut it according to what is possible for you.
And observe, so that you do not hit the artery, and does not happen a flow of blood, and the sick dies from that flow with the evacuation of water.
Of the incisions of arteries which are behind the ears.
Head 2.

Head

And the method of operation in extracting them, is, as the patient has hair on his temples, and it points to an apparent artery in the temple. And himself he shows you from his pulse, and rarely is hidden except in a few men, or when he shudders with cold.
If it is hidden from you, then the patient should tie his head with any cloth: and then he should cover the place with a rough cloth. Or he should moisten the place with warm water, until it appears to you in a manifest way. Then take a spikelet, which has been slightly bent. Then scratch the skin with it easily, until you reach an artery. Then throw it into her and extract it from above, until you draw it out of the skin, and make it ooze with sweat from tunics which are under it on all sides.
If the artery is thin: then wrap it up with the end of the spikelet. Then cut from that part a little more than the length of its ends, and turn them in opposite directions, and do not let there be any flow of blood. For if it does not cut, and if it does not split, the deep blood will not rise.
Then make ooze with blood for six ounces, up to three drops.
If the artery is large: then it should be tied in two places with double thread, strong, from silk: or with string of the hair, so that it does not come under putrefaction before hardening of the wound, and let there be a flow of blood.

Chapter IV.
On the treatment of acute, chronic, and stinging eye wounds.
When the tears are persistent and there is a course of blood from the veins that run along the outside of the skull: when this does not respond to medical treatment, his eyes will begin to turn red, and he will feel a crawling sensation on his forehead, as if it were caused by ants walking over it; his eyes will become dry and irritated, so they have been corroded by their hair with corrosion; and his eyelids will become heated from the pain of the tears. Then the ancient people used to treat them with this operation, and called it the Ense cure.
And is, as you command, to shave off the hair on the forehead of the sick. Then make three incisions in the forehead that are equally spaced according to its length: and let the length of each incision be almost as long as two fingers, and let one incision be equally distant from the middle of the nose, and the second according to half the distance between the two mandibular teeth, and the third from the side of the second: and pay no attention to the arteries that are on either side: and extend your hand out from the joint of the two jaws, and let the space between each incision be the length of three joined fingers: and have a sponge plug or a dry cloth ready for stopping up the blood.
Then introduce a long sharp instrument into the two ends of the incision, whose end is soon followed by this form: From the incision that is from the temporal side, all the way to the second incision: and scrape with it all the skin that is between the two incisions, along with the waxy membrane that is on top of the bone. Then do this also from the middle incision to the second incision. Then pull out this spoon and introduce into the first incision again a different instrument, which is called a sharp chisel from one side of the lather, not acute from the other side. And this is his form.
And this is his form.

§ On the treatment of acute tears and cataracts in the eyes from within the head.
When acute, sharp, and frequent tears occur in someone's eyes, and their eyes appear weak, pale, and already weakened: and the eyelids become ulcerated, and hair falls out from them, and there is a sharp pain in the deep part of the head, and resulting sneezing: then remove these accidents, so that those materials do not come, unless they are removed with many.
And the best treatment for them is this. And it is as you instruct the sick person to shave his forehead. Then separate between the two lips of the wound with a hot sponge, or with linen bandages. Then bind above with flannel: and dip the flannel in wine and oil so that a hot pus does not form.

Chapter VI.
Regarding the cure that falls on gold.
All that falls on gold is of four kinds: either mineral rock, or similar stones, such as iron and lead; or it is from a plant, such as chickpeas and beans; or it is a fluid, such as water and vinegar, and things like them; or some kind of animal.
When, however, a stone falls on gold, or a kind of rock that does not add to it, and does not grow in gold, expose gold to the sun: but if you see a stone, then distill into gold some of the oil of olive nuts, or sesame seeds. Then administer the extraction, and make it snort with ointment, and paint the nose at the approach of the snorting, after you have put on around the ears rolls of cloth or wool, and extend the ear towards the top.
For often with this cure one goes wrong.
But if he does not go wrong, then administer the extraction with gentle hand, that is, with thin gestures: whose form is this.
But if he goes wrong with his hand, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction with a thin, blind hook, made in a few places.
If therefore he does not come out through that [incision], then make a tube of brass, and introduce the end of the tube into the ear hole a lot, and the dust that is around the tube with the softened gold with oil, so that there is no way for the wind except through the tube: then draw it out with your breath strongly.
For many times he went out with it when we told him. But if it does not come out in this way: then take from the alum-pot or from the water, that is, the gluten prepared, with which gold is woven, a little piece: and put it on the end of the ear after you have dried the ear with moisture. Then introduce it into the ear hole easily, after you have removed the wax from the ear.
But if it does not come out with all that we have told you, then prepare yourself to split it, before a hot blister or spasm occurs.
And the way to split it is so that the phlebotomist takes blood from the head first: and draw out the blood according to the measure of its strength. Then make the sick person sit between your hands, and turn his ear towards the top, and find a small hole at the base of his ear next to his fat there: and make the hole round in shape, until you reach a stone: then take it out with that, which is possible for you from instruments.
Then close up the hole from your side with speed, and care for that, until it heals.
That if what falls into the ear is from one grain, which grows, and swells up: then administer its extraction.

Axirnath is a grease that is generated in the eyelids; and it often happens that this affects young people: it damages their eyes, causing them to have cataracts in the morning, and they cannot see the light of the sun, because their tears flow towards them, and for that reason they always rest their faces on their hands, and lie upon them when they sleep, and their eyelids are moist with an inflammation, which has already been caused by the swelling: and the protuberance of Axirnath is apparent to the eye; and when you press the spot with your fingers, you feel Axirnath between them.

Regarding the methods of Ataxmir for the eyes: that is, when the eyelid becomes soft to the eye, so that it rubs as it should not.

Chapter XII.
De the creation of two canisters for puncturing the eye with an aiguille.
The operation in that case is, that you should take an aiguille sharp, and stick it into the eye with a thread of silk. Then bind the ends together, and tie each with a small knot; and make the length of the threads be half an inch.

Regarding the incision of the nail and the eminence of the flesh of tears.
Chapter XVI.
You know that the nail is according to two ways. Or it is nervous: and it is similar to a soft, thin wood. Or it is not nervous, similar to frozen moisture as snow: which when it touches metal, iron, or tin takes it with a hook, and does not stick to it.
And both kinds do not begin, unless from the greater tear, until it is slowly discharged, until it dries up, and prevents the light, and the movement of the eye.

Then cut the residue on the lacrimal root with a fine scalpel, or with small forceps; and release the natural flesh of the lacrimal so that its course of tears is not interrupted by the incision.

Then, after the incision, pour into the eye some crushed salt, or make a paste of zinc, and leave it until another day. Then take care of the eye with whatever is necessary, until it heals.
