§ On the Cure of Alconey.
CHAPTER XXII.
This condition called Alconey, is not anything but the white accumulating in the eye, similar to water dropping down, and it itself is not.
And the method of treatment for it is, that you should make the sick person sit on a prepared bench, or directly.
Then take his head in your hands from both sides, and gently move it, until you feel the white moving to the lower part of his eyes. Then bind it, and let it not fall down, and make the light complete: and the sick person shall see as he used to; and if it does not fall down below, you shall know that it is water.
If, however, the descent of the white with it has not been prepared as we have said, then make the sick person sit between your hands. Then take a thin spatulum, and find it with him slightly above the connection of the corium with the corneal layer in the crown, until the white comes out.
So then when you have walked out, then distill into the eye hot water in which you mixed honey: or water in which you have already boiled fenugreek and honey; and then treat with the remaining treatment, until it is healed.
On the treatment of water that has entered the eye, or a cascade.
Chapter XXIII On the Treatment of Water That Has Entered the Eye
I have already spoken on the species of water, which are divided, and which suit the diagnosis and explanation, then take that same one according to the cure.
Then you should make the patient sit with his two hands between himself and the light, near the sun: and bind his healthy eye, and tighten it: then you can blink his eye with your right hand, if the water has entered his left eye: or with your left hand, if it is his right eye.
Then take alum with your right hand, if the eye is on the left: or with your left hand, if it is on the right.
Then put the end of the alum towards the crown by the thickness of the radius in the white of the eye which appears to be the tear: then push the alum with force: and you can turn your hand while doing so, until it penetrates into the socket of the eye: and you will feel that the alum has already reached the dry spot.
And it should be such a measure of distance for the alum to the depth, which is the space between the pupil and the end of the blackness: and that is the crown of the eye. You will see it in the same pupil with a red eye, on account of the clarity of the cornea.
Then put the alum until you reach the place where the water is. Then press it down with a gentle force.
But if the water has already descended, then the sick person will see it right away, and the alum in his own eye immediately.
Then rest a little. If water has fallen, then deposit it second, except for what has exited as almonds.
When, however, it is formed and does not rise up: then extract the Almonds with ease: and you shall move your hand gradually.
Then dissolve in water a little of the clear salt of the gem: and wash with it the inner eye. Then put on the whole eye a drop, or a wool dipped in rose-oil, and white of egg: and bind it with it the healthy eye.
But we, and those who are our companions at this time, put on him powdered cumin, mixed with white of egg.
That if the Almond does not obey you at the entrance to the eye through its durezza, since it is from a man, whose eye is very hard: then you should take the spikelet which is called Alberid, whose this form.
Open it then with him only the conjunction so much, and not the last your hand in the hole: and is there only to do you make a small space for the Almond.
Then introduce the Almond, according to what we have said above.
And at the completion of your work, let be prepared for the sick an uneven-made bed, in which he may sleep on his back in a dark house: and let be forbidden from all movements, and from coughing: and place before him food by which nature heals him: and let not move his head to the right, or at all to the left.
And let sit the ligature according to its position until the third day.
Then dissolve it in that dark house, and test his vision: and let him see objects. Then reduce the ligature until the seventh day.
But it is not necessary that he do this at the time of healing, or immediately after the incision: but rather, let him keep it away: because water rises quickly through a steep aspect.
If, however, the apoplexy is hot: then it is necessary that you release the eye before the seventh; and correct it with that which is settled when the apoplexy is settled: then absolve his sight, and put over his face the oral part in which the sight of him under lies for a few days, while he remains in that dark house.
Then let him leave the house gradually, and turn round in his seats.
And know that the student is not excused from sight sometimes in the zalah: then let him dare to look at the operation.
And indeed one of those who are from Al-Ayrah has already come to us; he said that it was done in Al-Ayrah a hole made with the magdan by which water is sucked up.
But verily you will not see anyone on earth who did that: and it is not written about him in any of the old books: and it is possible that it should be new.
And these are the forms of the eyes from the magdan, so that they stand on her who does not know them.
Let them be made of pure brass: and let their ends be with this same subtle triangular shape, and the acute end.
Head 24th.
Regarding the care of a birthmark on the nose.
When and what different meats are added to the nose, from which there is something that resembles a scorpion of many feet: and from it is that cancerous meat, stone-like in colour, which is soft; and from it is that flesh which is soft, not stone-like in colour.
In that which of these meats is soft, not deceitful, and not cancerous, you should make it sit between your hands opposite the sun, and open its nostrils, and throw in a hook made of thin sharp iron from one side; then pull it out to the outside, and cut off what you have caught with it by means of a fine sharp chisel: then draw it towards you, and see if all the meat has gone.
If anything remains that cannot be cut off: then cut it with a slender instrument easily, until nothing remains of it. But if blood rules over you, or a fever occurs: then oppose it with that which is necessary; or if it is a malignant abscess, then approach it by cauterizing it, until the blood is cut off and all the flesh is taken away.
Then let it be poured into the nose after an incision with vinegar, and water, or wine. But if the nose is opened, and moisture proceeds from it to the palate, then you should know that he is already well.
But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you should know that within himself there is a birth in the upper bones of the nose, to which the knife does not reach with the incision.
Then it is necessary that you introduce a thread of linen, of which there is some grossness, and spots in it many: and place between each spot the amount of a finger, or less: and he will be relieved, so that he lets one end of the thread into his nose with a ray, or with whatever is possible for him after he has done himself similar azur: and he should carry his odor, until it reaches as far as his throat, and he should come out onto his throat.
And often indeed do this boys like this in school: and it is a simple thing for him who wants to.
Then place the two ends of the thread, the end that comes out onto the nose, and the other that remains in the nose. Then also close the opening of the skin with the thread. Let him be until you know that the flesh is already there with the spots on the thread.
Then pull out the thread: and put into the nose after drying up of the blood a liquid that you soaked in Egyptian ointment: let him be for three days, or more, until the ointment eats away all that remains of the flesh.
Then put in the end of the nose a canula of lead, for several days until it heals.
If it needs more cure than to dry it up, use that.
For making the lavage, when it is distilled with oil and other medicines to the nose, make it of silver or brass: that it be like a little lamp, open-ended like a seashell: and its bore also.
And if you want to make a closed canula, like a reed.
And the shell of the instrument for making the lavage be full, fixed: which has a handle at the end, so that you hold it when you heat it with oil, or what you want to use and liquid things.
Head 25.
The Thelul of the nose often begins at the end and grows larger, and increases in appearance over several days until it appears like a festering wound.
And because of that, you should cut off all of its growth at the beginning of its appearance, and scrape it out completely. Then put over the place, or cautery, or burning medicine that stays in its place.
If the cutting then lags behind until it grows larger, then examine it, if it is hard and has a dull color and few senses: then do not touch it with iron: because it is a cancerous growth.
For often the eye that has cut into a person's head develops a large, evil growth on top of it from which bad things arise.
And if the growth is soft to the touch and not dull in color, and you see that the cutting may have reached its whole extent, then wash it with water that is cool and cut the person without fear or trepidation: and heal the place along with it by drying it up and constricting it, until it heals over.
Head and neck.
On sewing up the nose, mouth, and ears.
For when a break in the continuity of one of these cartilage pieces occurs, little operation is effective on it, except in some men.
It is necessary, therefore, when it has happened to anyone of these things, as you should consider if the bone is recent with its blood: and then gather the pain of the wound with a suture: then take care of it, until it heals.
And if the continuity of the solution has already separated the lips, and some healthy part has been made: then it is necessary that you remove all of its own skin, until it bleeds. Then gather the two lips with a suture, and tie them tightly, and powder them over the wound with dragon's blood, and olive oil, ground: and put over the powders a fragment of a plaster of diafinicon, and some other of a consolidated plaster: and leave it tied for two days, or three. Then dissolve it, and change the medicine: and leave it, until the threads separate by themselves. Then take care of the wound with ointment, until it heals.
But the method of the suture is, to gather the solution of continuity, or with the knuckles, as we have told you about the suture of the foot: or to gather the solution with a thread, as I have made you aware.
Head and neck.
The extraction of nodules from the lips.
In fact, it happens to many men, and especially in the inner lips there are similar hard little lumps of herbs: and some smaller, and some larger.
Therefore it is necessary that you open the lips, and find out on every lump, and hang it up with a hook, and drop it from all sides.
Then fill the place after cutting dry, ground, until the blood dries.
Then clean it with vinegar, and take care of the place with it, where there is a stinging sensation, until the wounds heal.
De incisione carnis natae super gingiuam.
Of the incision of flesh that has grown on the gums.
Often a sore grows on the gums, which the ancients called abluss.
It is necessary that you should hang it by a hook: or hold it with tongs and cut it close to its root, and allow the wound to discharge its pus or blood.
Then put on a place of poultice of ground pepper, or other astringent powders, drying agents.
That if that sore returns after treatment, for often it does return, then cut it again and causticate it: for this does not return after the cauterisation.
De rasione dentium cum ferro.
As regards shaving the teeth with iron.
When they have gathered on the surface of the teeth from within and from outside, and between the gums are rough, knots, and sometimes corroding them, and becoming yellow, and white, until the corruption reaches the gums, and the teeth are decayed by it.
It is necessary that you should put the sick person between your hands, and his head in your lap, and shave off the rotten molars and teeth on which you see the gums, and similar ground powder: until there remains nothing of it, and likewise do with the blackness, rustiness, yellowness, and other discolourations, until they are cleansed.
If then what is removed from them at the beginning of the shaving is good: and if not, then repeat the shaving another day, and a third time, until you have come to the last study in it that you wish.
And know that the teeth respond to various shapes of blades: and also, as regards preparing your operation, this blade with which you cut from below is different from the blade which cuts between the teeth, according to their shapes.
And these forms of blades are prepared for you, which you will see.
Chapter 30.
On the extraction of toothache.
It is necessary that he who seeks to extract a tooth should be very careful and diligent in its extraction and late in its eradication. For the tooth cannot be made to yield when it is eradicated: since the substance is soft; until, indeed, there is no excuse for its eradication, then let him who seeks to extract a tooth when he is ill consider eradicating it so that it hardens, and certify with you, the toothache.
Often the illness deceives the sick person and he supposes that the pain is in the tooth and eradicates it himself: then the pain does not retreat until the tooth is eradicated.
For we have already seen from the operation of bleeding.
Then, when the toothache is certified with you, let him who seeks to extract it scrape around the tooth with a file, in which there is some virtue, until it has healed the gum entirely: then, with your fingers or with delicate forceps little by little, until you have struck it.
Then, when the place is good and you have located it well, and your head is between your knees, which you hold firmly so that it does not move: then, with a firm grip, draw out the tooth according to its straight line, so as not to break it.
If then it does not come out, then take one of these instruments and push it under it from all sides with ease, and try to move it, as you did at first.
If then the tooth is pierced or corroded: then it is necessary to fill the cavity with cloth: and you should hold it tight with a narrow forceps so that it does not break at the time of your constriction on it with the forceps.
And it is necessary, that you should carefully examine with scraping around the gum entirely.
And keep your strength, so that you do not break it and a part of it remains, and returns to the sick one from that evil which causes him greater pain first.
And for that reason, do not do what the phlebotomators do when they are in a hurry and their boldness overcomes them in eradicating it, except that they administer it which we have said.
For this reason, repeatedly they bring about great illnesses in men, which are more difficult to break than to heal and leave all the roots of it or some of its parts; or take it out with some of the bones of the jaw: as we have been told many times that thing.
Then they wash it after eradicating it with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
That if it should happen that the flow of blood comes from the places (for it often happens) then dry up a little of the wound, and fill it with it: and if not, cauterize it, if it does not give you any relief.
The shapes of the forceps which move with subtlety in the first place are long at their ends, short in the handle, thick so that they do not double when pressed against the tooth: they are like the thick handles which you see, until when you press them together they do not bite into themselves, nor double; and the shorter ends, and they are made of iron ingot or a twisted bar of iron, straightened out: and in their ends there are teeth, some of which enter into some things, and by constricting them tightly, they hold fast with force.
And when the ends become like the shape of an ear which is called a ciconia, and are strong constriction:
Chapter 31.
of the eradication of teeth and extraction of fractures of the mandible bones.
When a tooth that is broken remains after eradication, then you should place it on the cot with butter for one or two days, until it softens: and then introduce into it the gouge or the forceps; whose ends are like an ear which is called a ciconia. The shape of this forceps is.
Make the ends smooth like a file: or like an awl.
But if he does not yield to you at the exit with these pincers, then you should cut off the root, and peel off all the flesh, and insert the instrument which is called a small palanquin, whose shape is this.
The short end should be slightly thicker; and it should not be wet, lest it break.
But if the root comes out by means of that, it is good; and if not, you should help with these other instruments whose shapes are these.
The shape of the first triangular end, in which there is some thickness.
The shape of the second triangular end, which is thinner.
And with the other instruments and tools which have gone before in the description of the teeth.
Also help with this instrument which is like a large hook, of the shape of the second triangular end, twisted, in which there is some thickness so that it does not break; and let it not be wet.
And know that there are many instruments for the teeth; and likewise the other instruments do not count; and the prudent artisan finds out by himself the instrument, according to which it is necessary for him to operate and to cure his own ailments.
For from the diseases of the teeth, there are instruments which the ancient ones did not describe, because of the diversity of their forms.
But if the jaw is broken by the molar, or by any other bone of the mouth, then examine it carefully in its place with what belongs to it from the instruments and pincers which I have described for extracting the root, and help with these gestures, whose shape is this.
Let it be slightly thicker so that it holds together, or let it be held with the jaw, and do not let it move or vibrate until the jaw comes out; and restore its place with the suitable medicines for it.
If there is putrid pus in bone then scrape it off and cure it until sound.
Of the dismembering of a tooth from the jaw-bone.
On the removal of the teeth from the jaw-bone.
When teeth become dislocated from their natural course, they get foul through the shape of the jaw, especially when it happens to women and girls, that is to say, young.
It is necessary for you to consider. For if one tooth has come after another, and does not fit into its place, or is possible to open it with a file, then scrape it out: and if it is joined with another tooth, then cut it out with this instrument, of which the following is the form.
It is like a little chisel, made of iron, with a sharp end.
And your cut should be deep so that it can go through the bone, and for the hardness of the tooth, and so that another tooth does not move.
If it is exposed by the wear of its own file: then scrape it with a file made of iron, of which the following is the form.
It should all be made of iron, and its little end pointed with the point of an awl, like a file with which nails are made: and with this the tooth is scraped little by little over several days with ease, so that another tooth does not move, and it falls off: then it is to be smoothed, in the end, scraped with some rasps.
If it is a tooth that breaks off a piece and hurts the tongue: then you must also smooth out this piece, until its roughness has gone, and make it even: and it should be smoothed, so as not to hurt the tongue, or damage the speech.
Chapter 33: Of the extraction of teeth when they are decay
Of the retaining of teeth when they are decayed with gold.
When the anterior teeth have a shock or movement by reason of a blow, or accident: and cannot hold firm on them, and they do not taste good after the use of medicines for their relief, then it is clever in them to fasten them with gold wire: because silver becomes yellow, and decayed after a few days: but gold does not change.
And let there be a thread medium in fineness and coarseness according to the quantity that it takes between teeth.
And the shape of the retention is so that you take the thread and insert it twice its length between two healthy teeth: then you knit it with its two extremities in a thread between the teeth of both parts until you reach the other healthy tooth. Then repeat the texture until you reach the side from which you began: and tightly with subtlety and wisdom, until it does not move completely: and let your constriction be where you tighten the thread, near the roots of the teeth, so that it does not move.
Then cut off the excess ends of the thread with the pincer: and gather both sides, and turn them towards each other: and hide them between the healthy tooth and the moted one so that they do not hurt the tongue: then let it be loosened in such a way that there is left only a small amount.
If however it loosens or cuts, tighten them with another thread and let it stand with it in such a way for a whole time.
And this is the form of the teeth, and the shape of the retention of two healthy teeth and two moted teeth as you see them.
And sometimes, when one tooth falls and heals again in its place, and the retainers remain as we have described, and do not hurt it - this is done only by a skilled, prudent, and experienced artisan.
And sometimes a bone is broken by a jab: and it is made like the form of a tooth, and put in place, from which it is protected and tightened, as we have said: and remains, and stays with it for a long time.
Head 34.
Sometimes this ligament that happens under the tongue is either natural with which man is born, or accidental due to an arrow that has already healed.
And the operation is, so that you open the mouth of the patient on his head in your bosom, and relieve his tongue: then cut this neural ligament across its width, until the tongue is released from its retention.
If there is something hard and rigid in it and it is a result of injury and the wound is healed: then insert a hook into it and cut across its width until you reach the ligament, and release the rigidity.
And do not make a cut at the bottom of the flesh, and do not cut an artery there, and do not cause blood to flow.
Then wash the incision with pink water or vinegar or cold water.
Then place under the tongue a lymph from linen, which holds the sick one every night: so that it does not become consolidated again.
But if there is blood flow, then place on the spot a lump of dried clay. But if you are pricked by blood, then cauterize the spot with a burning coals, which suits it: then take care of yourself with the rest of the cure, until it heals.
Head XXXV
When a little pustule forms under the tongue that absorbs the small wound, preventing the tongue from its natural function: and perhaps it increases so much, until the bone is filled up.
And the operation is, to open the jaw without pain by the sun: and consider the pustule.
But if you see that the color of it is dark or black, and hard, and the sick person does not have a feeling: then do not touch it, for it is cancer.
And if it declines to whiteness, in which there is moisture, then insert into it a hook, and cut it with a very fine scalpel, and free it from all parts. If you are pricked by blood during your operation, then place on the spot a lump of dried clay, until the blood stops: and then resume your operation, taking off the skin with its appendages.
Then wash with vinegar and salt: and care for that wound with suitable cure until it heals.
¶ On the treatment of abscesses of the two amygdaloids.
Chapter 36. On the treatment of abscesses of the two
When abscesses occur between the tonsils, that is, glands which resemble abscesses and occur in the jaw: they are called the two amygdaloids; when treated as described in the division, and yet do not heal, then consider.
If then there is an abscess that is hard, of a pale colour, with little sensation: then do not touch the abscess with iron.
And if it is of a red colour, and the root is thick: then do not touch it with iron, fearing that there will be a flow of blood; but leave it, until it has grown dry. And then either you pierce it: or it will burst of itself.
And if it is of a white colour, round, and its root is thin: then the wound should be allowed to bleed.
And the operation on it is such, that you should consider before the operation itself, if its abscess is hot, and has become quiet and complete, or is somehow imminent: then therefore make the person sit in front of the sun, and place his head in your lap: and open the mouth, and let him take hold of the tongue from below with an instrument, which has this form.
Let it be made of silver, or of brass, that it is fine like a knife.
When then you press with it on the tongue, and it shows itself to you, falling on your side: then take a hook, and fasten it in the amygdaloid, and pull it out as far as you can, pulling off some of the skin with it.
Then cut it with an instrument, which has this form following. It is joined with ligatures: however, its ends are curled up, so that the opening of each of them is on the acute side of the other: wherefore it should be so made of iron, or of a felled skin, that it may absorb.
If it is not present this instrument, then cut it with a chisel, whose this is the shape. Let it be sharp on one part, not sharp on the other.
And having cut one side of the amigdalon, cut the other second to this same form of incision.
Then after the incision gargle the sick with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
But if it happens that there is a flow of blood, gargle with water in which the skins of apples are boiled: or leaves of myrtle, and such like from stypics, until the flow of blood has stopped: then take care of the wound, until it heals.
And when ever there arise in the throat lumps, except two amigdalons. Then cut them as I said above for the cutting of the two amigdalons.
And I too have already treated a woman from an apostematous lump that was born between her throat and which she would put out into froth, little feeling, which had almost closed up her throat: and the woman breathed through my mouth, and had stopped eating, drinking water, and had come close to death, if it had remained one day, or two days.
And the lump had risen so much that it had thrown up two sprigs, until they had come out at two holes in the nose.
So I ran faster, and fixed my hook into one of them. Then I pulled it out, and a big piece came out with it.
Then I cut it off where it was caught in the hole of the nose.
Then I made it come out of the other hole of the nose.
Then I opened her mouth, and pressed her tongue: and then I fixed my hook into it: then cut off a part of it, and there was not much blood coming out: so the woman's throat is entirely stopped, and she began to drink water right away, and then took food to eat.
Therefore I have ceased to strike at that place for a long time; and the scar which I struck has given way to another, until it was too late and was joined to that one.
I therefore used cautery on the scar between the teeth.
So it stood firm from the addition; then I walked away from that part, and did not know what God did with it after me.
On the scar of the wound on the mouth.
Chapter 37 (head)
When the discharge comes down to the lip, and is scarred, and is long; then it is called a vertical scar; and if it is on the lower part and thick, round, then it is called a mole.
When cauterizing with it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not manifest itself; and you see that the scar has become cold from it, and is thin; then you should strike at it.
And what is joined to it that is round and has no length, and is bloody or dark-colored or black, and has no feeling; then you should strike off its scar. For fear is in the scar on the sick.
So you should do when you see it like the way I have described from whiteness and its length, so that you set the sick person before the sun; and press his tongue with an instrument which has gone before in narration: then fasten a hook into the lip, and pull it down: and strike it with one or two instruments which I have mentioned in cutting the two palates.
And you should not strike from it, unless it is added to the natural term without addition.
For if you strike from it any more, you will hurt speech and conversation.
Then after the scar has been struck from it, use that which I have described in cutting the two palates: and take care of it until it is healed.
But if the sick person trembles from the scar; then you should use your skill in cauterizing it without fear and worry.
The mode of cautery with her is not, unless with sharp water: and it is, that you put the head of the nurse in your bosom. Then press her tongue with the instrument which we have said. Then take from the water which I have told you in the chapter of cauterizing, and mix it with her foot not extinct, and put it not thick, nor thin, and fill it with this instrument, whose is this shape.
Sit at the end of her where the medicine is placed, as placed on the cochlea of the radius.
And place the instrument with the medicine on her uvula: and the sick lie on his side, so that the salve comes from her mouth from within the medicine, so that it does not go down from it to his throat, and hurts him.
Then take your hand with the medicine. And you from the first put it on her uvula of half-dose hour, until you see it has become blackened, and has calmed its itching with the medicine's mordication.
And if you want to take the cup and roll it on the end of the radius, and pour the cup with the medicine, and insert the radius with the cup into the tube from above, until it adheres to the uvula.
Do this many times, until you get what you want of the new cauterizing. Then let go of her: for she will heal and fall after three days, or four.
That if you want to drink the medicine, repeat it: and after cauterizing wash around her with a new cup dipped in butter, and clean with it what is in around her from the medicine: and let it sit with cold water.
And be cured from outside with embrocations, and inside with gargles, until he is healed.
This then species of cure is more beneficial than the incising and further distant from the fear.
And sometimes it is also cured with a sound that is finer than cautery and incision: for this reason it is cured with suffumigation, in this way. Take sumac, hyssop, oregano, rue, sseah, chamomile, abrotanums, and other herbs like them; put all of these together in a bowl, and add some vinegar and boil it: the pot should be well covered with litter: and there should be an opening in the middle of the pot above which a fine instrument is placed, as follows.
Let it be made of silver or brass; and the end, in which is the grain, should be inserted into the opening of the tube, until the steam ascends to the edge of the tube, until it is much obscured.
Then repeat this many times, until it is healed.
And if there is a wound, do not begin this cure at the very beginning. For it adds something to the wound: and you should not do this cure unless it is near the time of the warmth of the wound.
But if you do not have this instrument with you, then take a tube and fit a bit of wood to the end of it, so that the smoke does not burn the opening: for the wood prevents the steam from burning; and this is good cure with health.
Regarding the extraction of spine, and bone from the stomach.
Chapter 38 (on) surgery.
Many times an object like a tooth or a spine attached to the stomach, or some other foreign body.
Then, so that what is extraneous to it appears on the surface where the bite has taken place, having pressed the tongue with an instrument at the sun, and shown you what is inside,
And that which does not appear to you, or is hidden in the stomach, must be taken out before the food is digested in the stomach: for this will be effective with health. Perhaps, however, it will come out through the bile.
He should swallow the end of a rope, or the root of a lettuce, or chew dry bread; or he should take the end of a sea sponge that is dry and soft; and bind it with a string, then swallow it. When therefore he has come to the place where there are spines or an oss, and is drawn out, then he goes out.
But if he does not go out with it as I have said: then use the instrument of lead in this form.
Let it be thicker than the radius somewhat, and let there be a curved end at its end, which he may introduce into his throat with ease: and let him hold his head raised up.
And let him beware that he does not touch his epiglottis with his tongue, so that it should not give rise to a cough, and drive out the bone or the spine, or introduce the medicine into himself with his own hand.
But as for the sick person who is to be examined, this is better: through his knowledge of the site of the wound; and let him push below, or lift up his hand with the instrument upwards, all this according to the quantity that has been prepared for him, until he has gone out.
On the Extraction of Blood-Sucker.
CHAPTER XXXIX.
When you are treating with the blood-sucker, and he does not yield, consider whether there is a sore throat before the sun, or after it, when you press his tongue with the instrument that I have told you of.
But if your yawning falls on the blood-sucker, extract it with a small hook, or with subtle movements, and turn away from it.
But if it is not possible with them: then take a tightly-coiled tube, and introduce it into the throat as far as the throat; and then introduce into the coiled tube an iron that is ignited with fire. Make this many times over: and let the sick person refrain from all water for a whole day.
Then let him take a full wash with cold water and open his mouth into it; and let him put his own jaw into it and swallow nothing from it; and let him moisten the water with his hand for an hour after another. For a frog immediately falls when he feels the water.
But if he does not leave with him as we have said, then let him smoke the sick with ants or with an axe as a tool that we have used in smoking with it.
Do this many times, because he will fall himself.
And the method of operation in smoking is that you take a pot in which are fire-roasted frog legs and cover it with a lid, and make a hole in that lid, and fix the end of the tool in that hole.

Head II.
On the care of the eminence of the umbilicus.
Emancipation of the umbilicus is due to various causes. It comes out from the fissures that are above the navel: and it issues forth from it, either as anus or intestine, according to what happens in the other ruptures. Or from the blood that flows out of a vein, or from an artery, according to what has been said above. Or from the windiness confined within it.
But if, on the other hand, it comes out through a fissure that is sifac, and the discharge is dirty: then it is like the color of bloody pus: and it is slimy, without pain: and it seems to be in different locations. And if, on the other hand, it is because of the exit of the intestine: then its site is with that which we have described, more varied in character. When you press it with your fingers, it is hidden: but then it returns, and perhaps there is a sound with it: and it makes a lot of noise at the entrance to the wind, and a rumbling noise.
But if, on the other hand, it is because of humidity, it is slimy, then it does not hide when you press it with your hand, nor does it become tighter, nor does it get added.
If, on the other hand, it is because of blood, then with these signs appears a swelling that turns black at the edge.
But if it is because of a born flesh: then it is a grayish, thick, hard swelling, and it forms one unit in quantity.
But if it is because of windiness, then the touch of it is gentle.
And the operation in it is this: if you note that the prominent umbilicus is because of blood from an artery, or vein, or windiness: then you should refrain from treating it. For there is danger and fear in it, as I taught you in the chapter where I said that swelling comes because of an artery or vein.
If the prominent umbilicus is because of an intestine or a hernia: then you should order the sick person to hold his breath and stand with his arms extended. If, however, the opposite side is a blood vessel or an artery: then surround it very much. Then turn to your own operation. And take two needles and introduce two strong threads into them: and introduce the two needles around the one you have made around the swelling in the form of a cross, which you make penetrate.
Then tighten the swelling at four places on the needles: and if there is a vein, remove the needle, and let it rest until the flesh has rotted away: and let it fall of itself: or cut it off when it becomes thin and rotten.
Then take care of the swelling with the ointment as needed until it heals.
That if the prominence of the navel is from flesh inside or from moisture: then you should seal up the swelling, as we have said. And draw out the blood, or the moisture that has entered it.
Then take care of the swelling to make the place solidify.
Chapter LIII.

We have already spoken at some length about the types of cancer and how to treat it with medicine: and how to beware of treating it with iron so that it does not ulcerate: and we spoke about cancer generated in the womb, and about caution in its treatment.

For I cannot heal from it myself: nor did I see anyone else who has recovered from it.

The Extraction of Stone.
We have already spoken in the division of the species of stone, and the cure of it with medicines; and we have also distinguished between stone generated in the kidneys, bladder, and other parts, and that is operated on by hand or section: and this is stone properly generated in the bladder: and that which is generated in the kidney is that which grows on the stalk: and I am now speaking of it with manifest illustration and abbreviation.
I therefore say, as for stone generated in the bladder, it often happens to boys.
When a person's urine flows out of his penis like water, and it is thin, and there appears to be white sand in it, and the man's penis hurts when he moves it, and he suffers with it, and often hangs down: Then it becomes erect, and is discharged with the anus in many of them.
And the cure of boys is easy from that age until they are fourteen years old. And it is difficult in the elderly. But in young men it is half-way between the two; and the cure is easier if the man' s stone is large; and if it is small, then the cure is difficult for him.
When we come to the cure, it is necessary first of all that we should clean out the sick man with a clister, which he should remove all the dung that is in his intestines: for sometimes he prevents the discovery of the stone in the inquiry.
Then the sick man should be taken with his feet, and shaken up, and moved down: that the stone may go down into the depths of the rectum, or sometimes come out from a high place.
Then make him sit between your hands, prepared like this, and let his hands be under his heels, so that the entire rectum may decline towards the bottom:
Then inquire about it, and feel it from the outside.
If then you feel a stone in the space, immediately turn yourself towards the section above it.
If it does not fall under your touch at all, then you should wipe the index finger with the oil of your left hand, if the sick boy is a boy; or with the middle finger if he is a full-grown man: and put him in some part of his anus, and feel the stone until it is under your finger: and turn him slowly towards his anus.
Then press on it with your finger, and push it towards the outside against the section which you have found; and let one minister rub his hand on the anus, and another minister stretch out his right hand to the top: and let him moisten the skin, which is under the testicles in that part where the section is.
Then introduce the spatumil incidens, whose form this is. Then find in it what is between the anus and the testicles, and not in the middle, to the left of the birth: and let the cut be made above it, and your finger be in the anus: and let the cut be made transversely, so that it is wide outside, and tight inside, according to the quantity that it is possible for the stone to come out from there without being bigger.
Perhaps the finger, which is in the anus at the time of the cut, will press against the stone during the cutting, and will come out without difficulty.
And you should know that from the stone there are angles and edges, for this reason it is difficult to get out.
And from it there is something smooth, similar to a gland, and round: and the exit of it is easy.
So then to those who have angles and edges, add a groove.
If it does not come out in this way, then you should make use of: or stretch yourself over it with a wobbly gesture, whose end is as the Moon, which stretches over the stone and does not slip from it: or you should introduce under it a slim instrument, with curved ends.
If you cannot stretch on top of it either, then slightly enlarge the hole. That if something from the blood wins over it, cut it off with a scalpel while it is bleeding.
If the stone is more than one, then push into the first big one towards the anus. Then cut on top of it. Then push a little after it: and do likewise if there are more than two of them.
That if it is very big, then the cut on top of it will make it come off. Since this thing has happened to a man of the two things, or that he should die, or that he should have frequent urine passing: soon afterwards, because the place does not consolidate at all.
But give it an expulsion, until it comes out: or devices in the split of it with pincers, until you pull it out quickly.
When you have finished your operation, then fill the ulcer with thure, and aloe, and dragon's blood: and bind it well, and place over it a cloth dipped in oil and wine, or in rose-oil, and cold water: that so the pustule may be dried up by heat.
Then wrap the wound around the neck, and do not sever the ligature until the third day. When you have severed it, then smear the place with much oil and water.
Then care for the wound with the ointment of dye-fungus, and with the ointment of basilicon until it heals.
But if a warm pustule has been added to it, and it has corroded and there are similar things: for example, if blood has congealed in the bladder, and urine is prevented from flowing out of it: and it is known by the exit of blood with urine. That if the stone is small and lies in the meatus of the urethra and is embedded in it, and prevents urine from flowing out: then care for the stone with it when you come to a section of it. For often after this cure, there will be no more difficulty in passing water, because I have tried it out many times.

Head LII.
Regarding the cutting above the hernial opening with water.

Head 99.
§ On castration.
You know that castration is excommunicated by our law; and for that reason it would be well if I should not remember it in my book here; and the remembering of it is not necessary except for two reasons.
Of which one is, that it may be in the knowledge of the physician when he is questioned about it: and so that he may know how to cure him who has had it happen to him.
And the other mode is that we often lack castration of certain animals for our own benefit through it, such as goats, horses, and cats, and similar from animals.
I say then, that castration is done according to two ways. Or by friction. Or by a slits and sections.
In that which is done by friction the course of operation is this: that we make the animal sit in warm water until his testicles become soft and loosen and hang down: then we strike them with our hand until they are completely broken and do not appear under the touch.
In castration however by a slit and sections, you must hold the animal, and press the skin of his testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspenders and dry completely on all one section, until when the two balls come out: then open them after you have dried them both, and do not let slip anything except the thin skin, which is over the scrotum.
And this mode of castration is better than that which is done by friction: for friction may leave some of the testicles behind, so that the animal desires to have sex.
Heal then the fracture until it heals.

This then is what should be understood in the science of obstetrics. For it may perhaps come to that which is similar to it: then oppose it with it that which is necessary
Chapter LXVII.
On the extraction of a dead fetus.
When you are concerned with the extraction of a dead fetus as I have said in the division on surgery and do not exit, and you urge that you use the hand operation, then you should consider.
If then the woman is of sound virtue and is not with any of the accidents from which she fears destruction: then it should be that the woman reclines on her bed, on her back, and has her head inclined downward, and her legs raised: and he should hold her by two sides, or tie her to the bed, so that her body is not extracted along with the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the mother's mouth with moist oil with mucilaginous althaea, and fenugrecum, and flax seed.
Then the midwife should wash her hands with these oils and mucilages: then she should enter the woman' s womb with ease. Then she should ask where to place the knot of the fetus, and the suitable places for it.
Then consider, if the fetus is prepared to descend over its head: then place the knot in her eyes, or her throat, or her mouth, or her palate, or under her beard, or in her neck, or in the places adjacent to the ribs, and beneath the hip bones.
If however the descent is over his feet, then in the chest, and his ribs in the middle.
And it should be that he holds the awl with his right hand: and lays the wound on himself between the fingers of his left hand: and inserts with ease, and fastens the awl in one of those places which we said, until he has reached the hole.
Then fasten on the other side of his awl, or a third, if you are able to: so that it is equal contraction, and does not decline to the side.
Then let it be extended with an equal extension, and does not extend only according to the rectitude, but also move on all sides, so that it relieves his exit: as happens when a tooth is removed in the process of extraction.
And should be in him who is between that, so that the extension is softened. That if a part is retained from him, then it should be that the midwife puts some fingers with oil, and inserts them on the side, so that they rotate with it, because it holds.
If then a part of the fetus comes out, then change the awls to another place that is higher: do this until the whole fetus has come out.
If then a hand comes out ahead of the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by coarsening: then should be that a cloth is wrapped over it. Then draw it out until when all is coming out, cut it or insert it into the socket of the hand, or into the bed: and so should you do to the other hand, and to the two feet.
If then the head of the fetus is large, or has a coarsening during its exit, or there is water in his head: then should be that it inserts between the fingers of the Spatulimile spinosum, and finds with it the head, and draws out the water: or breaks it up with an instrument called Almisdach: whose shape comes with the forms of other instruments in the following chapter.
Similarly, if the fetus has a large head, then the umbilical cord should be cut: or else it should be pulled out with the hand, as we have said. Then, pull out the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out, and the cord is around the neck: then cut off, until the moisture which is in the chest is let out.
If it is not complicated, and does not submit to delivery: then cut off the head prematurely, as far as you can do it.
If the lower limb is deformed, or there is hydrops in it: then you should cut off the member, until the moisture which is in it has run out.
But if the fetus is above its feet, then the attraction of it is easy, and the direction of it towards the mother's mouth is gentle.
But if the cord is around the gut, or the chest: then you should take a piece of cloth which you have on your hand, and cut off the member, until the moisture which is in it has run out.
If other limbs are also taken away, and then the head comes out: then let the midwife put her left hand in. But if the mother' s mouth is open, then let the woman put her hand in deep into the vagina, and look at the head, and attract it with her fingers up to the mouth: then let her put in a hook, or two hooks, and attract it with it.
If the mouth of the mother is closed, because of the hot swelling which has happened to it: then it is not necessary that she should work on the fetus, but rather at that time you should administer to her the flowing fluids, thick: and apply plasters: and let her sit in water which softens and moistens.
If the fetus is above its side, then it is possible that it will be quiet: then administer to it what we have said about a single fetus.
If it is not possible to do so, then incise quickly and remove it.
And you should not leave anything inside at all after the second incision.
Since you have completed your operation, then administer what we said in the apostemes of the hot things that happen in the wombs.
If a flow of blood occurs, then let it go down in water of rigor, and administer the remaining cure.
And I have already seen a woman, in whose womb the fetus was dead: and then she became pregnant again on top of that same womb, after which the other fetus also died. So it happened to her after a long time that an apostema appeared in her navel, and it swelled up until it was opened, and it began to discharge pus.
So I was called to her cure, and I treated her for a long time: and the wound did not heal.
I then placed over it some strong adhesive plasters: and it came out of place from the mouth. Then a few days passed, and another outlet came out from her mouth. I was amazed then that there is no outlet in the womb when there is an outlet in the mouth.
I thought, since there are bones of a dead fetus.
I inquired about the wound, and I pulled out many bones, while she was in a better state of health: and now she did not live for such a long time, and she began to discharge pus from the site little by little.
And I do not make this foreign to you, unless there is knowledge and aid for it, which the skilled healer can administer with his hand in the cure.
Chapter LXVII. On The Head.
On Forms Of Instruments Necessary For The Extraction Of The Fetus.
The form of the jaw opening.
Here is the form of the Strigulator, which are joined at equal intervals to two rods, with two twines. However, this vertigo should be made less coarse than the striga, and so it is made either of ebony or of wood from the buss tree.
And let the width of all the wood be as wide as two fingers: and the margin of each of them is as wide as a finger, and their length is as a palm and half; and in the middle of the two woods there are two additions of the same kind of wood, which have already been set firm on both, the length of which is the half of the palm and slightly more; and the width of each is almost two fingers, or slightly less.
And these two additions are inserted into the jaw bone, so that it opens with them when you turn your two wheels.
There is another one similar to it, which is smaller and lighter.
Let it be made of ebony wood, or pine wood, according to the similarity of the claws. However, at the end there are two additions, as you can see here above: and the length of each of them is almost a palm: and the width of each is that of two fingers.
But when you open the jaw with it, then make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging down, open what is between her shoulder blades. Then insert these two additions joined together into the jaw: and you, holding the end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument as you do with the claws, equally according to the quantity that you wish by opening the mouth of the jaw, until the midwife does what she wants to do.
The form of the second wheel, which is different from that which the ancient people spoke about, as it pushes forward the fetus.
The form of Al-Misdar, by which the great head is turned: and resembles the claws, with teeth at the end, as you can see.
And when it is turned inwards, as the claw does according to this form, as you can see, with teeth like a saw, which cuts and turns inside.
Form a Vncinis with one spine.
Form a Vncinis with two spines.
Form a scissor with two ends for cutting off the head.
Also form two scissors for holding open.
These instruments are all used and the more their kinds multiply and they are prepared for use by artifice, the quicker they are in their work and the higher they stand among men because of their number.
Do not then despise these instruments, even if they do not exist with you; rather, have them prepared for you. It is not excusable to need them.

§ On the Extraction of the Second.
When the second is retained at childbirth, then you must take care to hold back the weakling so that it does not hold its breath. Then make her sneeze with a squeeze; and tightly grasp your hand over her nose. If then she comes out through this, it is good.
If not: then take a club, and pierce through the roof; and put in it herbs opening the mouth of the mother, such as calamus, rue, aniseed, camomile, chamomile, and cassia bark, and some of these herbs; and dip them in water, and place them on the fire.
Then put a twig of hawthorn on the hole in the roof, and another end at the mouth of the mother; and let her hold it until the steam from the birth has cooled down.
Then make her sneeze, as we have said. The second is then born with ease.
If, however, it remains after this care and does not come out: then instruct the Midwife to dip her hand in sesame oil or mucilaginous aloe. Then he inserted himself into her vagina and inquired about her second birth. So when he found her, then he took her, and he slowly stretched her out.
But if she is attached in the depths of the womb, then he should insert his hand, according to what we have said above, until such time as he finds the second one and gradually pulls it out according to the straightness so that the womb does not fall due to a sudden pull: at the front it should be exchanged with ease from right to left: then it is added in quantity. For she will obey then and spread herself out, and she will separate herself from the adhesion.
That if the opening of the womb is constricted, as we have already related: take care of it with a sternutation, and from the medication of the wound with herbs.
But if she does not come out with all that we have said above, then take care not to tire her out in the process of extraction.
But it is necessary for what comes out at the opening of the womb from her to be tied up on the woman's thigh. Then clean her with a four-part ointment. For this will make her rot and dissolve after a few days, and she will come out.
But when it is rotten, a bad smell comes out of it towards the stomach and head, and it hurts that part. It is necessary then that appropriate suffumigations be administered to her.
Some of the ancient ones who have already been experienced are the suffumigations of mustard and dried figs.
Form a tool with which to suffume the woman during the retention of the second birth and the months.
Let it be made from a similar wool or from hemp: and let it be placed on a wide end over fire: and the suffumigation should be placed on plums: hold it, until that suffumigation is consumed: and then take another one.
Chapter LXXIX.
As for the treatment of women who have not been penetrated.
Many boys were born, and their hams were not pierced, which the sutures of the delicate sirocco had already opened. It is necessary that the midwife pierce that sirocco with her finger: and if she does not, she should pierce it with a sharp spatulim: and let her beware of touching the snake, lest she be bitten.
Then put a woolen cloth, soaked in wine and oil, on top of it. Then care for the wound with ointment, until it heals.
But if you guess that he is drunk, then put a lead plunger in the hole for many days, and remove it when the boy wishes to defecate.
And it also happened that the boys were drunk because of the concusiveness of the wine or pus. It is necessary that you remove that consolidation, and then care for it with the above-mentioned things after removing it.
Chapter LXXX.
Regarding the cure of fistulas that occur in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are a nodding and grossness which occurs near the anus of a particular animal: or in the space of one part: and there is one fistula, or many.
When that grossness is cured, it opens, and from it issues a watery moisture of white pus or a subtle pus.
And when they are penetrating from these fistulas. Thus the penetrating ones are recognized by that which issues from defecation, and their wetness, when a person with an illness defecates: and perhaps they issue from them naked.
And there are fistulas from which they penetrate into the space all the way to the bone, and up to the vertex of the hip. And some of them penetrate all the way to the joint of the hip, and up to the root of the tail.
From that one from which the penetrating fistula all the way to an animal is recognized, and also not from a non-penetrating one, is, when you put your index finger into the anus: and try to push a thin piece of metal or brass into the fistula: if there is no tortuosity.
If there is a twist in it, then insert into it a thin probe, or a nail from the nails of the equines, until you feel it trying, or a nail in your finger.
If you do not feel it thoroughly, and there is no discharge from the wound, nor any pus, nor is it as I have said: then know that it is not penetrating: therefore approach again to the cure.
And when the fistula penetrates as far as the skin, or to the bladder: then the sign of it is the flow of urine from it, and its prohibition from this so that the place with the medicines consolidates.
If it penetrates as far as the joint of the hip, or to the jaw: then the sign of it is that it reaches with a probe as far as there, if there is no twist in it up to the jaw: and there is pain on the circumference of the part, and pus always comes out from it: and that it does not scar with ointment, and consolidates.
And in all these fistulas which penetrate completely there is no cure at all: and the cure of them is work and vanity to him from foolish doctors, on whom a form is made up.
In that one, or if it is not penetrating, and is not ancient, there is hope for a cure with a knife: for I tell you, and I have tested this myself: and it is, so that the sick man lies in your hands on his back: and trim the legs of him up to above his hips, and his hips are bent towards his venter. Then insert a probe or air, if it is a twist fistula, until you know where the probe reaches.
But if he feels it on a certain part, then you should put your finger on that part.
But if you feel the probe already penetrate itself by your finger, besides that you feel it between your finger and the skin, or flesh: then know for sure that it is penetrating: so do not work on it, because its cure is not as I said.
They said that he heals some people's flesh, and from the medicine which he hopes will benefit them, it is as if he sets fire to a cautery of fine fire according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before, and he inserts it in the fistula until it reaches a certain point. Then he does this again twice or three times, until you know that all the added filtered flesh, which is like a feather, has dried up and become similar to a feather.
Then he cares for that with liniments soaked in butter until the dried-up flesh comes out: and then he cares for it with ointments that generate meat and consolidate it.
If then he heals, it is good.
And if not, then he does not heal with any other cure ever.
And if it comes out and does not reach your finger, which is in the anus, and is between it and a hard piece of flesh or a blade: and you see a fistula on it that follows the skin's surface, then dry off the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and dry out with the towel what is in the fistula, until you reach the place where the end of the towel reaches, and let the towel fall and drop.
Then clean those filtered flesh, which are like a feather, so that nothing remains of them.
If however the blood hurts you, and dissolves between you and your surgery so that it solves those flesh: then it is better if it happens, and quicker in its benefit, to cauterize it with fire, or with sharp medicine.
For the cautery with fire brings good habits together, to the burning of that flesh which is added, and to the stopping of blood, and drying up of moisture.
Then he cares for that with liniments soaked in butter, or with crushed leaves, until the place gives off pus, and dried-up flesh comes out in the pus.
Then the cure for the scar when the wound has hardened with ointments, producing hard flesh: and there are medicines in which are stigmatis and drying out.
For when it is being treated, then it is being healed: and do not put off repetition.
But if the fistula has reached to a great depth of the anus, and has elongated from the excess fluid of the body: then insert your finger into the anus, and feel with it.
But if you feel a pulsatillenesse and between yourself and her is some kind of a defect, or flesh, and is near to penetration: then there is no operation in that, unless by the second time of confidence and hope.
That is, because it is done in him one of the two ways: or as it is cauterized itself, as we have said: or separate it, until the consequence of its concavity comes about, so that it is possible for you to introduce a scalpel, and cure from nearby. And do not proceed much with the incision, lest you fall into the trap of the continous anus, and happens on to a premature death of exhaustion without will. Then the cure for that with him which we have said.
Perhaps it will be healed: or will elongate the defect, and clean it up all the way to near the anus, as we have said, or with a probe, or with another acute end of an instrument. Then clean those filthy meats which are in the incision, all the way to where you can with examination.
Then try to restore the wound of the whole limb with the incision, and the opening where it hardens: and remains a fistula open on the inside part of the anus, and will be lighter on to the premature death.
And when the fistula follows this way: and is, when you introduce a probe into the fistula: and is on the side of the anus near to the surface of the body with skin and the margin of the anus: then take hold of the probe's sharp end, which is like an accusative, that is, a preparative tool, according to this form. And introduce into it a thread uncoiled from five threads, and wrap it around. Then introduce the thread with a hook into the fistula, until you feel its tension.
If then it is penetrating into the margin of the anus internally nearby, then remove the thread from that opening: so that you can introduce your finger in anum, and remove the end of the thread, and gather both ends together at once: and tighten both of them, and let it go one day, or two days: and to the extent that the thread bites into the flesh, tighten it well, until those muscles which are between the two ends of the thread fall down: then take care of the wound, until it hardens, and heals.
If, however, the opening of the fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate in whatever way you prepare it for yourself, unless it is in a deep place. For indeed it is not yours to do such a thing, so that you don't hurt yourself itself.
Then do with it as we have said, until it heals.
The shape of the sharp needle where the fistula is found, whose curvature is acute greatly, and its other side is not acute, so that it does not hurt that which is not necessary, as you see.
Chapter LIII.
Of the suture of hemorrhoids, from which runs blood from their incisions: and take care of the fissures.
There are hemorrhoids according to two ways. Or indeed they are inside the anus, similar to charcoal, or like plums: or almost like small grains. And of them there are some little ones and some big ones: and blood runs from them always, and there is one, and many. And they are outside the anus, and at its ends.
Indeed these that are outside the anus, are according to most part few of moisture, from which runs yellow water, or a little blood with constant course: and they are according to color of the body.
And the cure of that which is within the anus, you should instruct the sick person to straining; and it should be expressed until it comes out, and appears atheneum to you. Therefore therefore and hang with hooks: or hold them with your fingernail. Then therefore cut them at their roots.
If however they do not retain hooks, because of their moisture and their own softness: then take them with a rough cloth, or with a twine made of double-twined wool, and pull them out with your fingers. Then cut them and sprinkle over them after the cut some warm powders so that they remain in place of cauterization. Or cauterize them according to what has preceded in the chapter on cauterizing. Then care for them with the remaining cure, until they are healed.
That if the anus does not obey the ejection, then clench the sick with a small clister in which is a little mordicatio, so that it soothes with it what is in the ano, and obeys the ejection more quickly when it is expressed by the sick.
If however atheneum have been taken out of the ano, then the business is lighter and easier: and it is as if you were to take them with your fingernail, or take them with a hook, and cut them. Then care for them with what we have said, until they are healed.
And who hates cutting with iron, then you should administer to them a sutura in the following way. Take a silk thread, and insert it into the anus. Then pull out the atheneum upwards, and let it penetrate with the needle into the root from the other side; and wrap the two ends of the silk thread around the lower part of the needle, and spread them out: and tighten the atheneum with a strong knot. Then tie off the silk thread, and pull out the silk thread.
Do this to all the atheneum, and leave one alone: and let his own be drawn out, so that it carries away the redundancy of blood.
Then put a certain cloth soaked in rose-water, or neroli-water, on the part; and put the same on the part itself; and order the sick one to lie down. Then let him lie down until he has fallen asleep.
When the wound has therefore closed, take care of them with ointment, and with the other treatment, until they are healed.
§ On the treatment of wounds. For often accidents happen because of drying up of stool, and constriction of nature.
When they have been a little while wet, and do not suffer from medicine: then let them be scrubbed with the sponge of Spongia, or with your own finger, until they are moist, and let go off them the upper layer which prevents their being consolidated. Then take care of them, until they are consolidated according to what is necessary.
But if they do not consolidate: then repeat the scrape with a more rough sponge than before, until they bleed much, and then take care of them, until they are healed.

Know that Almirmar is only a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to a claw's head: and it happens in the whole body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers: and it causes pain on walking.
Then let it be cut off what is in the circumference of the claw, and held with forceps, or with a hook, and Root it out from its root.
Then take care of that one: and if you have a caustic, treat it according to what has gone before in his chapter.
But from the sore-mouth there is only one little excellence, rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And often it happens in the hands of boys.
And its treatment is, that you spread out the sore-mouth, and let it fall; or that you tie it with silk thread: or with hair, until it falls down. And if you see [a wound], cauterize it according to what has been said above with fire, or with sharp medicine; and now the athelias that are imposed are eradicated, and not imposed with an instrument that I call.
But the ant is also a prominent little filter, coarse, on the surface of the body, wetting it deeply; and when it comes to coolness, it feels in it a similar stinging of an ant, and becomes in the whole body; and much of it is made in the hands.
And its cure is that you take a tube from the beak of a goose, or a strong vulture's beak; and put that tube on the ant, until it holds a circle of the tube from its parts. Then you will turn your hand with the tube, until you separate what is in the circumference of the ant; and put it in the depth of the flesh, and you eradicate the ant from its root.

The large clister.
Cistere paruum.

On one side there are two openings, and on the other side there is one opening.
And many holes are pierced in the cysts, as it were, and there is a space that is the width of a finger between each hole. When this cloth is placed in the cysts, tighten it in the top part of the cysts with a strong knot between two distinctions. Then tighten the cloth.
And this is the shape of a circle as it is depicted here, and the holes.

Then remove the cloth, and raise the sick person's legs up towards the wall.
If medicine can save him to the end, then he should hold on as long as possible. And if he sleeps with her all night, it is even more of a last resort in healing.
