On the treatment of dislocations.
A dislocation is the exit of some joints from their place. Why it is prevented by its own motion, and is fixed in position. And does happen to cause great pain and painful wounds.
But when such a dislocation has happened, then let it hurry to restore it: and do not delay it at all.
For if it is delayed, the place will be infected, and there may well be a recurrence of the dislocation with it.
Therefore, it is not appropriate for him to move or extend himself at the time of examination. Because he often causes a spasm to occur and hurts with his movements.
But when that happens, then you should approach the wound with care. Then he should be dismissed until the swelling subsides.
Then the member is to be warmed with warm water and oil. Then it is to be reduced with ease.
And all members are to be cared for with their respective treatments.
I have already arranged the chapters on dislocations, also regarding the prior fracture, from the upper part of the body to the lower.
§ On the treatment of a dislocation of the lower jaw.
The two jaws are rarely dislocated.
And the dislocation of the lower jaw occurs in one of two ways. Or, on the other hand, they move away from their places by a small distance and become slightly softer. Or they are dislocated with an intact and complete dislocation until they become soft to the breastbone, until they salivate with care, and they cannot hold it, nor can they close their mouth, and their tongue is extended with a hiss.
When, however, the dislocation of his jaw is small, then it returns to its place by itself with a little difficulty.
But if the dislocation is complete and intact: then it should be administered to reduce it quickly, and there should be no delay: and it is as if the doctor held the head with his hand at the base of the jaw's dislocation between its teeth, if the dislocation is from one side. Or introduce two fingers simultaneously, if the dislocation is on both sides. And the remaining fingers of his hand are outside, which makes it even.
And recommend to the sick person that they clean their jaws and allow them to eat fully. And the surgeon should make the jaw equal and push it back to its place.
If it is difficult to reduce it, especially if both jaws are involved: then administer perspiration with warm water and oil until the reduction becomes easy: and do not delay the reduction of the jaws at all, as we have said.
When they have healed and been made equal, and the jaw has closed, and the swelling has not subsided: then place a few cloth pads on them, with a ball of wax that has been made from wax; and oil rosin.
Then it is bound together easily with soft ligaments.
And it should lie down on its back: and the head of the patient should be placed between two cloth pads so that it does not move to one side or the other: and it should not be forced to chew anything: but its food should be soft, so that when the pain goes away, the jaw can open: then it may eat what it wants, and administer it easily.
It should not be troubled by the operation of its mouth during eating and drinking, and whistling, until the jaw has healed and become well.
If it is difficult to reduce the two jaws when they are dislocated at some time, and do not return to their places: then frequent fevers and sodas occur: and perhaps intestinal congestion occurs, and perhaps pure choler is lost.
So when you see this: then know that it is a sign of death, and many times that person dies within ten days.
On the reduction of dislocation of the furrow and the extreme of the arm.
The furrow does not dislocate from the side due to the continuity of its connection with the chest. And it dislocations when and where it goes outwardly: and announces this to the sense.
And its restoration is so that it lies sick on its back, and extends its arms. Then bind the place with your palm and bandage it strongly, for itself will come back.
Then put a plaster on it, and poultices, and tighten it.
The extremities of the leg, which follow the hip, and continue with it, are rarely dislocated, unless by rare chance. If it is dislocated on any day: then let it be reduced and adjusted according to what we have said, and that you be prepared.
Then put a plaster on it, and poultices, and bind it tight. And command the sick person to adhere to peace and calmness until he is healed.
And with this same treatment the limb of the shoulder blade is reduced when it separates from its place as well.
On the Reduction of Dislocation of the Shoulder Blade.
You should know that the shoulder blade is not dislocated unless by three means.
One of which is that it dislocates to the tickling side toward the lower part. The second is that it dislocates to the side of the chest. And perhaps it dislocates to the upper part of the shoulder blade: and this is rare.
And does not dislocate to the rear due to the spatula. And does not dislocate to the front due to the nerves.
Indeed, it is very often that the shoulder blade dislocates and comes out towards the lower part next to the tickling: especially in those whose flesh is scarce. Because it exits them quickly, and enters them quickly.
But in those whose flesh is abundant, the opposite happens to it: that is, because it exits with difficulty, and enters with difficulty.
And perhaps happens to certain people a blow or a fall, and the shoulder blade comes out with heat: and it is thought by them that this is because it has already been dislocated.
Therefore, let it be known to you, so that you do not hesitate about this, until you are completely certain of its state, and then proceed with its treatment.
And it is known that dislocation takes place when it turns downward in relation to the nipple: and you distinguish between a dislocated shoulder and a healthy shoulder. For you can clearly tell the difference between them: and dislocation in the head of the humerus, and under the nipple at the touch of the head of the humerus as if it were itself: and the weak cannot bring his hand to his ear, nor move it in all its movements.
And likewise, if it is dislocated towards the chest or upward: then there is a distinct touch, and it is not hidden.
And of this dislocation, its reduction easily takes place when it is young, or the boy is weak.
And its reduction is, as he raises his hand towards the top. Then put your fingers under its nipple, and raise the joint with strength towards the top to its place: and the boy raises his hand, and extends it upward. Then let him put it downward, for he himself will turn it back quickly.
If he does not turn back through the above-mentioned means, and there have been many days since dislocation took place: then it should be, so that the weak man bathes in warm water, and applies a remedy which softens and relaxes, such as if they were cooked roots of aloes, and fenugreek, and mallow in water, and is applied.
Then the weak man shall lie on his back: and a sphere and wool be placed under its nipple, which is equal between relaxation and constriction.
Then the doctor shall place his heel on the sphere, and raise the head of the humerus with strength, and draw the nurse's hand downward.
And if you wish, reduce him according to this method: and it is as if you are present man who is longer than the weak one, and stands by his side, and places his shoulder under the nurse's nipple: and raise her nipple upward, until the weak one hangs in mid-air. And another assistant should hold the patient's hand at the base of his foot. But if the sick person is light: then it should be that with him something else is suspended so that he does not move it: for the dislocation comes back immediately.
And it is also reduced in another way: and this is that it is fixed on the ground a long piece of wood whose head is round figure: like the sleeve of the mortar: which should not be thick or fine. Then put under the sick person a cloth made of soft material after it is placed on the head of the wood: and let the sick person stand according to the length of the wood.
Then the assistant extends the patient's hand at the lower part of one side, and he extends his body with strength from the other side: for the connection returns to its place with speed.
That if it is difficult to reduce him by all that we have said, then use this care: and this is that you take a piece of wood whose length is the length of two arms, and its width is the width of four fingers, and its thickness is the width of two fingers: whose head is round, so as to relieve the entrance into the hollow, according to this form.
Then they bind on the round head a soft cloth so that it does not hurt the wood of the sick person.
Then put under the tickling assistant so that it extends the hand or arm over the wood to the lower part: and the wood is tied over the assistant's hand and arm and the end of the finger.
Then put the arm over the step by its width, and extend the hand at the lower part, and let the rest of the body be suspended from one side. For the connection enters immediately.
Since then it is finished entering in whatever way possible: then you should put under the tickling sphere of equal quantity of wool. Then place the preparated plaster made of powdered rose with olive oil and white resin on the whole shoulder, as it comes down from above.
Then tighten the bandage under the pressure of the swelling: and return the ligament over the splint above: and join his hand to his neck, and let it be, and do not move his hand for seven days.
And it is necessary that he take a little food for the sickly, until his member is healed: for it is quicker to heal him in this way.
Then it should be placed more widely after seven or five days, and he should be tested with movement. If then it remains stable and does not weaken, then he is now healed.
If on the other hand the joint dislocates many times, because of the moisture that occurs with it, or because of some other cause: then it is necessary, in order to administer cauterization with six pores, as was said in the chapter about cauterization.
What if all of this is done, and the ligament is allowed to heal over seven days, and the joint does not remain dislocated, and the splint and constriction over it are sometimes loosened, and does not firm up, and falls away, and he cannot raise it up again to his shoulder: then you should know that the nerves which are to the shoulder have already been cut, or extended, or weakened: and you should know that the joint will never be set in its place.
But if the dislocation is towards the chest and nipple, or towards the rear, it is done by an impact and extension with the hands: until it stops, and a remaining constriction and care is administered to it, until it heals.
What if after healing a little weight comes on the member, and there is a delay in its movement: then the sick person should take frequent baths, until this weight is softened, and return to its natural state first.
The Treatment of Dislocation of the Elbow.
You should know that the elbow joint dislocates with difficulty, and also heals with difficulty: it actually dislocates in all directions, and especially to the front, or to the back.
And his dislocation is not hidden from you: because it falls by sight and by touch, whatever form it takes. And when you join the dislocated hip with the sound one, that will be evident to you. For the joint will ache, and it cannot duplicate the arm, nor can it touch its shoulder with it.
And you must hurry to reduce the dislocation as soon as possible before the injury swells.
For if the injury swells, it is difficult to reduce it; and perhaps it will not heal at all, especially when it is behind. For every form of dislocation is worse, and the pain from it is more severe; and often death comes with it.
And the restoration of it when it has been reduced as much as possible is, that he extend his hand with two hands; and his arm be stretched out, and his fingers on either side of the hip, or on its root, pushing at the dislocation with the thumbs of his hands until he returns to his place.
Or perhaps the dislocation is forward: then he returns in such a way that he duplicates his hand with his own, striking at the hip which has been dislocated with the root of his palm until it hurts.
Which if it does not obey the reduction, then administer a fierce, sharp extension; and it is as if two ministers extended his arm: and let them hold him too, so that he does not move during the extension.
And then his arm turns around to all parts after it has been wrapped over its hand with a long cloth, or with a broad strap.
And when the doctor touches the dislocation with his own hand, he should wet it with oil so that it is from those things that help to lubricate the joint with ease. Then push the dislocation with a sharp thrust until it returns.
And after its reduction, it should be placed on it a plaster that has the staphyloma and drying with alum, and it should be tightened by a thightening as it goes down. And hang the arm from the neck of the nurse; and let it go for a few days.
Then let it be unbound. But if the joint is secure in its place, then untie the ligament from it, and let it go.
And if you see that the joint is not well tied, then put on more plaster and the ligament, and let it go for a few days until it is tied. Then let it be unbound.
But if it comes to pass that he has lost his weight after the reduction of the joint, and the position is in motion: then administer humidity in the bath, and subtle friction, and compression, until it is healed, or put iliac on the joint, that is, nates arietis pinguem. Then tie it up, and let it go on top of it for a day and night. Then remove it, and let him enter the bath. But when he sweats, then apply friction to the joint with a moderate friction. Then put on top of it oil a single time, and a second time, and a third time with the entrance into the bath, until it is relaxed.
And if there is a wound, put on top of it cow dung, moist, heated with butter, and tie over it.
Perform this several times. The joint is healed, and returns to its position.
This is the treatment of dislocation by Albucasis.
Mahassem sometimes dislocates, that is, the joint between the arm and the hand.
And the reduction of his dislocation is easy. On the contrary, the joints remain in their places. However, it should be that the speed is in the reduction of his dislocation in the hour in which it dislocates, before it has been measured: or happens in it a hot apoplexy.
And the reduction of dislocation is in it, so that you put Mahassem's hand weak on a table, and extends his servant hand: and the doctor puts his palm on the eminence of the joint, and pushes it, until he has set it back.
Indeed, it should be considered that if the palm has already receded to the abdomen of the hand: then the sick person should put his back of the hand on a table at the extension and reduction: and if the dislocation is proceeding towards the back of the hand, then the position of the hand should be placed intrusively over the table, that is, the interior part of the hand over the table should be placed so that the doctor's hand falls upon it with emphasis on the tendon.
If it then returns immediately, it is good: and if not, then bind it with a plaster while the swelling subsides: and let him go, and do not return to it.
For if he does not bear it, and you cannot bring it to reduction after a few days, then the tendon remains according to its curvature: and it does not hurt the sick person unless his hand becomes soft, and he cannot grasp anything: then you should know that the nerves have been cut or worn away.
Therefore, there is no skill in it except to bind it with a wound close to its danger. And perhaps it does not give anything.
But when Albucasis does not return, then put on him a plaster which we have described. Then let it be bound and let it be left for five days: then let it be loosed and let it be exercised.
But if its movement is restricted, and something heavy happens to it: then soften it with warm water and occasional friction, until it becomes soft.
On the treatment of dislocation of the fingers.
When one of the fingers is dislocated completely, or one of them towards the back of the palm, or towards its heel: then extend that finger, and push the dislocation with your thumb until it returns.
Then support the head of the finger and hang it towards the side to which it is dislocated, and let him go for two days.
Then hang him up and extend him, until he is even with his back on that day.
When then the night having come, bind him according to his story: and do not cease to loosen him on that day: and exercise him with movement: and bind him in the night.
Make it for those days, until he is bound.
And also do the same with him, if his hand goes out of place: and bind him to that side, and do your first work with him, until he is healed.
And also do the same with him when his dislocated to other parts.
On the treatment of dislocations of the spine.
When it happens to anyone that the spine is dislocated, or when many of the joints are separated from their places: then there is no cure for it, because death approaches the sick.
And the sign of it is that he who is sickly leaves his bed without choice, and cannot hold it: and often weakens some member of him, or two legs of his, or two arms of his, or one of them; or when one of his spine joints is separated from its place.
For it often happens that they are separated again, since they are separated on the four sides.
So then who is dislocated backward is called a hunchback.
The cure for it however is that you consider then if the hunchback happens from infancy: then there is no cure for it, nor is there at all healing from it.
But in that which happens by fall, or by punch, or similar to those, the ancients have already said long words of ways of cure. Whose most does not return with profit.
I however have shortened that out of it, whose little excuse from a great distance from my nearness to intention: and my exposure which I exposed that, and I shaped an instrument from him in different ways from him so as to show that, and they showed him.
I therefore say that in the deformity which occurs from the anterior part, there is no art and no cure from it.
And likewise in that which happens on both sides as well.
And let it not be cured from them unless that which happens in the back of its own, with what I am telling you: and it is as if a sick person extended on his face on an equal platform near the wall: and spread out under him a wet cloth, so that it does not hurt his chest.
Then let a straight wooden beam be fixed in the ground, at the end of the foot, around the head of it: and another wooden beam around his feet at the other end of the foot: and let the servant hold fast to the beam, and not be firmly planted in the ground. And let another servant hold fast the other one.
Then let the nurse turn round on top of his head and under his chin with a soft band, firm: and spread out the end of the ligament to the wood which is at his head: and bind himself there.
Then let another ligament be tied above his shoulders and above his knees and near his ankles. Then let all the ligaments be gathered together and bound to the other beam which is at his feet.
Then let all the servants extend to the side of the beam and not remove the two beams from their places where they are fixed: however, they should not be firmly planted, as I said.
Then let the doctor place his palms on the spine with strength until he recoups: or let him place it on the board. Then let him join his feet to the board until he recoups.
If however he does not recover by this cure, then take a board whose length is about three arm-lengths. And make a hole in the wall from which I spoke, which is near the sick person, a place to which the end of the board enters. Then let half of the board be placed on the spine. Let the physician set his feet upon the other end. And tie it well, until the backboard is fitted, and return to your own place.
Then if you wish, operate with the turner that is held in your hand: and it is so, to put two pieces of wood on the ground near the head of the bed, whose length are the length of one arm; and near the head of those two pieces of wood.
And the length that is between all the wood be one palm: and there has already been made a hole, in which the turner runs; and all the wood is made firm on the ground so that it does not move at all.
And a round piece of wood be introduced; and there is a turner in which the ligament turns in two holes of the two pieces of wood.
And at its end there is a hole, in which the wood is fixed, whose length is one palm with that in which it turns; and it is the same in the other two pieces of wood.
Then tighten the ligaments that you have tied inside the chest of the turner that is by its head: and the ligaments that you have tied in his legs in the turner that is at his feet.
Then stand by all the turner, who twists his hand with a lever, with which it turns; and the physician adjusts the backboard, according to what we have said.
This is the form of the turner, which follows.
Then, when the backboard has returned and the place is made equal, then you should put dried blood mixed with albumen on the wounds. Then the stain. Then place above the blood a board from a table, whose width is three fingers wide, or about that. And its length to take up the space of the support, and on the healthy side of the backboard.
Then it is tied with a ligament that we have said. Let the sick one be fed with subtle food until he is healed.
If anything remains of a disease in the place at the end of healing: then it is necessary that which softens and makes mild be administered, with the tablet that we mentioned for a long time. And now it is administered in that tin-plate.
And when there is a disease at the very end of the spine: and it is thought through that dislocation, and it is this jaw that has already begun to emerge. Why should not the presumption be made with this medicine: for perhaps such will happen that it may cause death.
On the cure of an ankle dislocation.
You should know that the ankle joint, and the shoulder joint, do not occur unless there is a dislocation only: and they do not occur to them what happens to the other joints because of a small distance, and urgency.
And the ankle joint dislocates according to four parts. Because it dislocates to the front and to the back.
And many times it dislocates inwardly: and little to the front, and to the back.
And the cure of its dislocation inwardly is: because when you join the thigh of the sick with a healthy one, it is longer: and it is the genuflexion of him prominent than healthy, and cannot the sick double his leg by himself: and there is a place that follows the coxa separated apart, for this reason, that the head of the thigh has already reached there.
And the sign of him who has a dislocation to the outside is, that are opposite accidents to these accidents.
And the sign of him who has a dislocation to the front is, that he expands the healthy thigh according to the complement: however, it does not double itself without pain which is in the knee: and if it tries to walk, it cannot pass over that to the front: and it retains his urine, and is separated from the groin of him, and there is a trodden upon his heel when he walks.
The sign of dislocation to the back is that the knee does not bend before doubling the leg and also because the thigh becomes shorter on the other side; and the kneecap is at the place of the hip joint.
The reduction of this dislocation is that you consider then, if the dislocation is old, which now has healed with the one who had it. Then, if you administer the reduction of it, and it remains according to its position: then it is not at all in this treatment. Therefore, it should not be presumed that he has a complete cure.
But in that one whose dislocation is recent, and is of the four types of dislocations: then approach to this, that you rotate it, and extend it towards the inside and outside, and move it with the right and left hand: perhaps it will return, and does not need another treatment.
But if it does not return in this way, then you have to prepare strong medicine, and extend the thigh from its lower part: or with his hands, or with a ligament that is tied above the thigh over the knee: and another servant extend his hand on the inside of his thigh so that he inserts his fingers under the skin of his thigh. Then tie it with a soft ligament over the root of the hip, and hold the end of one of the ligaments.
And let him sit in an extended position or from the front part of the groin to the thigh, or from the back to the spine.
And let all these extended positions be made in one way, until he stands up with his body from the ground, and remains hanging.
This type of extension is a common type among the four types of dislocations.
If this dislocation returns with what I have said, it is good, and if not, then it is necessary to say about each type that I speak of as its own cure.
In the reduction of this dislocation, when the dislocation is towards the inside, it should be, that the sick person lies on his healthy side. Then put the ligament on top of the root of the thigh, in that which is between the head of the thigh, and the place which is under the groin. Then extend the ligament to the top from the part of the groin to the higher part of the body, to the part of the thigh.
Then another strong minister should take his arm, and make small the place of the weak thigh, and extend it to the external extension in a mighty way. For he has already returned to his place.
And this type is easier than the other types of cure, because this limb is reduced in this way.
But if he does not obey you at all with this type of cure: then it should be, that two nurses bind him together with a strong ligament, soft, over the two heels, and over the two knees: and let the length of each from its own place be the same as four fingers: and let the leg be extended by the other quantity of two fingers.
Then the sick person should be hung on top of the ligament, which is in the house: and let his length from the ground be the same as two arms.
Then command a strong man to support the head of the thigh: and another should hang with the sick person: and another should push with strength, because the joint returns to its place with velocity.
In return, however, when it is dislocation to the outside, it should be, that he lies on his back, according to which we have said, having a gibbosity. And let the ligament be stretched over his thigh, his own, and over his chest.
Then two woods should be put, one at his feet, and another at his head. Then a wood should be put in the middle of the foot, firmly fixed: and let there be placed on it moist cloths, so that it does not hurt the sick person: and let the wood be between his thighs, so that it is not drawn toward the lower side at the extension.
Then all the attendants shall go to their respective places, and the doctor shall give the patient a thorough examination with his own hand.
If he complies with the request for reversion, it will be good.
And if not, place a table above it, and press it equally, as we have said in the case of deformity, However, he should lie on his sound side.
And when the dislocation is to the front, then it should be extended quickly with the help of an attendant: and this is according to what we have said about the stand: and the doctor shall place his right hand on the hip of the patient. Then he shall be pulled by the left hand, and with that pulling he shall be made to extend to the lower side of the leg.
And if the dislocation is to the back: then it should not be extended to the lower side, and he should sit on the ground; but it should be placed on a hard surface, as we have said, and this is also what we said about his lying on two backs: and this is on his face, and the extending ligaments: according to what we have just mentioned.
And it is necessary that compression with the table be applied also to the place from which the suture has been taken, when the reduction has been completed in accordance with what is required.
And the sign of his return should not be hidden from you: and this is when you extend the two legs of the attendants: and when you see them equal, and the patient tightens his leg, and opens it without excuse: then you shall know that his limb has returned, according to what is required; then join the two hips, and put a splint, and bind with bandages, that is, with rope: so that it does not move from one part to another: and let him remain quiet for three days, or four.
Then solve the ligaments, and the splint, and bring the legs together: and when you see them equal in position, then you shall know that the dislocation has been固固的。
If you see anything that softens: then return and cover it with a plaster and tighten it according to your first measure: and also let it go for three days.
Then dissolve that and make the person walk a little on both sides for several days, until he is well.
14. Of the dislocation of the knee-joint.
(3) The knee may be dislocated  (3) in three ways: (i.e.  (1) to the outside, (2) to the inside, and (3) to the bottom, i.e., to the back.
(And it is not dislocated (4) to the front.)
And the sign of its dislocation is (that he applies his knee to his hip). (But if it does not attach with the hip), then you shall know that the knee has been dislocated.
(And the restoration of all kinds of dislocations is this: to make the sick sit upright, so that he may stretch out his leg over it and attach his back to his face; and place his foot between your feet.)
Then fasten the knee of the person with the palms of your hands, and keep them straight between your fingers above his knee. Then apply with both palms of your hands to the sides of his knee with determination. (And another person extends his leg), until he brings back the knee to its place.
(The sign of restoration is) when the leg attaches to the hip with ease, not with effort.
Then cover him with a plaster, and make the leg attach to the hip. Then bind them together at the same time (for three or four days). Then dissolve them.
(And do not let the sick person walk a little for several days), until he is healed.
(But if you do not restore its reduction to you), then administer a strong extension with the ligaments, of which there is a report in the healing of ancient ankylosis, until he is restored.
On the treatment of dislocations of the calcaneum.
When the calcaneum is sometimes moved by a slight movement, and when it is sometimes dislocated from the second complement. And this dislocation of its takes place, either towards the insides, or towards the outsides.
And the sign of this dislocation is that you see the calcaneum swollen, protruding towards the side to which it is dislocated.
The treatment for this removal is simple and consists in returning it with ease with the hands, and in making it stable, until it returns to its place.
In the cure for this however, when it is dislocated from the second complement, you should make the sick person sit upright: and hold it firmly by a strong minister from behind its back, in the middle of its own.
Then hold it with your right hand from the upper part of its foot, and with your left hand from the lower part of the foot in the place of the nail.
Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand. Then, with the two joints of your left hand.
Then extend it with the left, and push the chest of the foot towards the leg without working.
Make it do this twice, as we have described.
Then push the chest of the foot towards the leg in a third pull, and you draw the nail in.
If it then returns in a single pull, or in two pulls according to this method, and you see the foot even, it is good; and if not, then repeat the operation on it: for it will return again.
But if it is forbidden to you to return it with that which we have described: then let the sick person lie on his back on the ground, and fix a firm footstool on the ground so that it may fall between its knees: and you may now draw up on top of it by means of a cloth, so that it does not hurt the sick person.
Then let the minister take the knee of the sick person: then extend the other minister's foot, or with its hands, or with a bandage which he ties above the knee of the foot. Then let all the ministers stand against his extension, and a pacifier be standing between two hips holding him back, so that his body is not drawn to the lower ones at the time of extension.
Then let the doctor make his hands equal and the other ministers hold the healthy leg down. For the dislocation returns with speed.
When therefore the dislocation returns, and it is declared to you that the return of health is made: then put on a plaster and a splint, and bind it firmly with ligaments, and tie the foot with a ligament to the leg.
And you should be careful and not fear about the nerves that are above the heel behind, so that there is no crushing of them by the ligament, and they hurt them.
Then let him go for two days, or three. That if the ligament softens, bind him: then solve him on the third day, or fourth: and prohibit the sick from walking for forty days. But if it attempts to walk before that space, there is no security unless the dislocation is dissolved on him, and it corrupts, and does not receive after it any cure.
That if it happens to him a swelling that is hot: then you should administer to him in seduction that which we have mentioned in another place from the cure of a swelling, and a poultice, until it moves away.
Of the dislocation of the fingers of the foot, and its cure.
It should be so that it is dislocated from them with a little extension without work: and this is not difficult, it is even easy.
But if the dislocation is in certain nods of the back of the foot: then it should be so that the sick person puts his foot on an equal place of the ground, or on a table: and he stands as one who walks.
Then you stand still, and put your foot on that which comes out from them by the joint. Then put that stone with your foot with strength, until it returns, and the hernia itself is already even, and does not seem to be outstanding in place.
Then put under the abdomen of that foot a plate which catches the whole foot, which has two heads. Then tighten it with a string to be worn for three days. Then solve it, and let it rest from walking for many days, until the string is tight and secure from the reduction.
As for the species of dislocation with a fracture or break.
When something like this has happened, and the patient is concerned about his cure and recovery, often death follows: and for that reason you should not presume to control his cure, which is of this kind, unless you are prudent in the art of long use, merciful, considerate, slow, not bold, nor presumptuous: and use medicines which sit on the pulse only, and let go of the sick with divine judgment. Except you hope for salvation from destruction with mildness of disease, and in which there seems to be some hope. Therefore consider the reduction of it at once at the beginning of the thing, before a hot poultice has happened.
If then the limb returns, according to our instructions, then administer a regimen which sits on the poultice: and attend to the wound with that which suits it from an ointment of dried herbs.
That if the dislocation is with a fracture, and have happened in bones separated from each other, then consider the removal of them, and make in it what we said in simple diseases because it has preceded in places of them.
And cause according to your strength, and protect yourself from the entrance into a trap of fear: because my prediction has come to you.
For that is better for you with your Creator, and more lasting to your glory, and more healthy to your body with them in your time.
